This Week in Apps,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/this-week-in-apps\/\">the weekly TechCrunch series<\/a> that recaps the latest in mobile OS news, mobile applications and the overall app economy.<\/p>\nThe app industry continues to grow, with"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/07\/app-stores-to-see-record-consumer-spend-of-133-billion-in-2021-143-6-billion-new-app-installs\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">a record<\/a> number of downloads and consumer spending across both the iOS and Google Play stores combined in 2021, according to the"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/07\/app-stores-to-see-record-consumer-spend-of-133-billion-in-2021-143-6-billion-new-app-installs\/\">latest<\/a> year-end"https:\/\/www.appannie.com\/en\/insights\/market-data\/2021-end-year-mobile-apps-recap\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reports<\/a>. App Annie says global spending across iOS and Google Play is up to $135 billion in 2021, and that figure will likely be higher when its annual report, including third-party app stores in China, is released next year. Consumers also downloaded 10 billion more apps in 2021 than in 2020, reaching nearly 140 billion in new installs, it found.<\/p>\nApps aren\u2019t just a way to pass idle hours \u2014 they\u2019re also a big business. In 2019, mobile-first companies had a"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/15\/app-stores-saw-record-204-billion-app-downloads-in-2019-consumer-spend-of-120-billion\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">combined<\/a> $544 billion valuation, 6.5x higher than those without a mobile focus. In 2020, investors"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/13\/app-stores-saw-record-218-billion-downloads-in-2020-consumer-spend-of-143-billion\/\">poured<\/a> $73 billion in capital into mobile companies \u2014 a figure that was up 27% year-over-year.<\/p>\nThis Week in Apps offers a way to keep up with this fast-moving industry in one place with the latest from the world of apps, including news, updates, startup fundings, mergers and acquisitions, and much more.<\/p>\nDo you want This Week in Apps in your inbox every Saturday? Sign up here:"http:\/\/techcrunch.com\/newsletters\">techcrunch.com\/newsletters<\/a><\/strong><\/em><\/p>\nTop Stories<\/h1>\nApps celebrate Global Accessibility Awareness Day<\/h3>\nThis past Thursday, May 19, 2022, marked the 11th Global Accessibility Awareness Day (GAAD), which is a day focused on raising awareness about digital access and inclusion for the more than 1 billion people who live with disabilities or impairments. A number of app makers and tech companies took part in GAAD this year to either highlight or announce new features designed to better meet the needs of those with vision impairment, hearing loss and other disabilities.<\/p>\nInstagram’s"https:\/\/about.instagram.com\/micro_site\/url\/?click_from_context_menu=true&country=US&destination=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.instagram.com%2Fcreators%2F&event_type=click&last_nav_impression_id=1CdGKXYlYDe4E0lHE&max_percent_page_viewed=64&max_viewport_height_px=650&max_viewport_width_px=1440&orig_request_uri=https%3A%2F%2Fabout.instagram.com%2Fblog%2Ftips-and-tricks%2Fadvancing-accessibility-on-instagram%2F&region=noam&scrolled=true&session_id=0CY7cymmK4zmFenWR&site=instagram_about\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">@creators account<\/a> shared information with its community about how and why to use accessibility features, like alt-text and auto-generated captions to create a better experience for your audience. The company"https:\/\/about.instagram.com\/blog\/tips-and-tricks\/advancing-accessibility-on-instagram\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">also noted other developments<\/a> it had rolled out, like dark mode, screen reader improvements, improved automatic and custom alternative text options for people with vision impairments, caption stickers for Reels and Stories, and more. The company also said it has started rolling out closed caption features to improve the Instagram experience for the deaf and hard of hearing communities. These changes help to improve the experience for everyone, however, as Instagram said one-third of video plays on Instagram are with the sound off. In March, Instagram made"u_0_c_aa\" class=\"_8ow9 _9gii\" href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/instagram\/status\/1498710216585613314\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">"_8-vl _8-vp\">"_95iu _8iqw\">auto-generated captions the default<\/span><\/span><\/a> for creators, which are supported globally across iOS and Android.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nGoogle shared its approach to both hiring people with disabilities and building products to meet their needs. For example, it highlighted projects like"https:\/\/blog.google\/outreach-initiatives\/accessibility\/project-relate\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-onclick=\"{"event":"page interaction","category":"in-article links","action":"link click","label":"https:\/\/blog.google\/outreach-initiatives\/accessibility\/project-relate\/"}\">Project Relate<\/a>, a communication tool for people with speech impairments; the update to"https:\/\/blog.google\/products\/android\/all-new-talkback\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-onclick=\"{"event":"page interaction","category":"in-article links","action":"link click","label":"https:\/\/blog.google\/products\/android\/all-new-talkback\/"}\">\u00a0TalkBack<\/a>, Android\u2019s built-in screen reader; and the"https:\/\/blog.google\/products\/chromebooks\/accessibility-features\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-onclick=\"{"event":"page interaction","category":"in-article links","action":"link click","label":"https:\/\/blog.google\/products\/chromebooks\/accessibility-features\/"}\">improved Select-to-Speak<\/a> Chromebook tool; a multi-pin feature for Google Meet, which allows users to pin multiple tiles, like a presenter’s screen and interpreter’s screen. The company also noted all its English-language YouTube Originals content from the past year \u2014 and moving forward \u2014 will now have English audio descriptions available globally.<\/p>\nApple, meanwhile, participated in GAAD with a number of"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/apple-adds-live-captions-to-iphone-and-mac-plus-more-accessibility-upgrades-to-come\/\">announcements<\/a> about"https:\/\/www.apple.com\/newsroom\/2022\/05\/apple-previews-innovative-accessibility-features\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">new accessibility features<\/a> for iPhone, Apple Watch and Mac.<\/p>\nThese included a universal Live Captions feature, improved visual and auditory detection modes and iOS access to WatchOS apps. Live Captions will be able to transcribe any audio content, like FaceTime calls, video conferencing apps and streaming video, as well as in-person conversations, all in English to start.<\/p>\n"attachment_2322399\" style=\"width: 1970px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2322399\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2322399 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1960\" height=\"1102\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg 1960w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg?resize=680,382 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1960px) 100vw, 1960px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2322399\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Apple<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nApple’s Sound Recognition feature will be able to be programmed to recognize sounds unique to a person’s own home, like their doorbell or appliances. The Magnifier app will add a new ML and lidar-powered Door Detection feature within a new Detection Mode section. This will help users locate a door, understand how far they are from it and describe door attributes. Apple Maps will offer sound and haptics feedback for VoiceOver users. And Apple Watch will help users control Apple Watch remotely from their paired iPhone with Apple Watch Mirroring. It also gains new Quick Action like a double-pinch gesture to answer or end a phone call, dismiss a notification, take a photo, play or pause media in the Now Playing app, and start, pause or resume a workout.<\/p>\nSnap’s platform policies for third-party apps aren’t yet fully enforced<\/h3>\n"attachment_2167646\" style=\"width: 3210px\" class=\"wp-caption https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/snapchat-speed-blur.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/snapchat-speed-blur.jpg?resize=1536,864 https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/snapchat-speed-blur.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 3200px) 100vw, 3200px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2167646\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nA handful of Snap Kit platform developers"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/snapchats-stricter-policies-for-anonymous-apps-and-friend-finders-arent-yet-fully-enforced\/\">have not yet complied<\/a> with the new guidelines around anonymous messaging and friend-finding apps"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/following-suicides-and-lawsuits-snapchat-restricts-apps-building-on-its-platform-with-new-policies\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">announced in March<\/a>. The Snapchat maker revamped its developer platform policies on March 17, 2022, to ban anonymous apps and require developers to build friend-finding apps to limit access to users 18 or older. The policy changes were effective immediately and existing developers were given 30 days to come into compliance \u2014 a date that would have passed last month.<\/p>\nIt is now mid-May and some developers of the newly banned and restricted apps are not yet meeting Snap\u2019s new requirements.<\/p>\nSnap confirmed to TechCrunch a small number of apps were given extensions, including anonymous apps LMK and Send It. But others seemed to be working around Snap’s ban with their friend-finding apps marketed to users ages 12+, instead of the now required 18+. They got away with this by not actually using the SDK — something impossible to tell from their App Store marketing and screenshots which imply they’re directly integrated with Snap’s features. Another app had flown under the radar, continuing to operate in violation of the rules unless TechCrunch pointed it out, resulting in a belated ban. This lack of clarity on which apps are platform apps, and which are only pretending to be, could complicate things for Snap, which is engaged in litigation over bullying-related suicides. And like all social media, the company could be under new U.S. regulation related to child safety matters in the future, as well.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Bd2UjCgxsR\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/snapchats-stricter-policies-for-anonymous-apps-and-friend-finders-arent-yet-fully-enforced\/\">Snapchat’s stricter policies for anonymous apps and friend finders aren’t yet fully enforced<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Snapchat’s stricter policies for anonymous apps and friend finders aren’t yet fully enforced” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/snapchats-stricter-policies-for-anonymous-apps-and-friend-finders-arent-yet-fully-enforced\/embed\/#?secret=e39VRJvFjG#?secret=Bd2UjCgxsR\" data-secret=\"Bd2UjCgxsR\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\nTwitter deal still a go… for now<\/h3>\nFirst,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/13\/elon-musk-twitter-deal-on-hold-spam\/\">Elon Musk tweeted<\/a> that the Twitter deal was “temporarily on hold” until Twitter could prove the percentage of spambots on its platform was actually less than 5%, as it reports. This Tuesday, he"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/elon-musk-twitter-spam\/\">reiterated<\/a> the deal would not move forward until Twitter would show him proof of this <5% figure. Twitter was having none of it, though. The company filed a"https:\/\/www.sec.gov\/Archives\/edgar\/data\/0001418091\/000119312522152250\/d283119dprem14a.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">\u00a0proxy statement<\/a>, saying it’s committed to the deal as agreed and is ready to close “as promptly as possible.”<\/p>\nIf Musk’s move was an"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/opinion\/articles\/2022-05-17\/elon-musk-does-not-care-about-spam-bots?sref=gni836kR\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">attempt to renegotiate the price<\/a>, it didn’t seem to be working. Twitter’s top lawyer and head of policy, Vijaya Gadde, told staff at an all-hands meeting there’s “no such thing as a deal being on hold,” reported"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2022-05-19\/twitter-deal-is-proceeding-not-on-hold-executives-tell-staff?sref=gni836kR\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bloomberg<\/a>. Twitter execs also suggested that it could try to enforce the deal terms in court, if need be, but said that would be “pretty rare” for such a thing to occur. (Not that this Twitter deal is proceeding normally though!) There’s still some speculation that Musk is looking to fully back out and will find a way to do so, billion-dollar breakup fee notwithstanding. In the meantime, the bankers are"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2022-05-18\/as-musk-tweets-advisers-plug-away-to-keep-twitter-deal-on-track\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">still preparing the paperwork<\/a> and execs are"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2022-05-17\/twitter-loses-three-more-senior-employees-ahead-of-musk-takeover?sref=gni836kR\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">still leaving<\/a>. This week, it was Twitter Service VP Katrina Lane, head of data science Max Schmeiser and VP of product management Ilya Brown — all of whom chose to leave on their own.<\/p>\nApple\u2019s new rules let apps raise subscription prices automatically<\/h3>\n"attachment_2133289\" style=\"width: 3210px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2133289\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2133289 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"3200\" height=\"1800\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg 3200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 3200px) 100vw, 3200px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2133289\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nAlongside the launch of the iOS 15.5 update, Apple introduced a new set of rules to govern auto-renewing subscriptions on the App Store. Now, instead of asking users to agree to any subscription price increases, developers will be able to roll out a price increase with the user\u2019s explicit consent. The feature allows developers to simply inform customers they\u2019ll be charged more, but not require the customer to opt-in to the higher pricing.<\/p>\n"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/05\/apple-pilot-tests-feature-that-allows-developers-to-automatically-charge-users-for-subscription-price-increases\/\">We first broke the news that Apple was pilot testing this program<\/a> last month, when it appeared Disney+ subscription customers had simply been told their price was increasing but weren\u2019t asked for their consent. Apple then confirmed this was the result of a \u201cnew commerce feature\u201d it planned to launch soon, which it said would be \u201cgreat for both developers and users.\u201d<\/p>\nApple\u2019s position is that this could save customers the hassle of having their subscriptions automatically canceled just because they didn\u2019t see the notification or email that asked them to opt in to the price increase.<\/p>\n\u201cThis has led to some services being unintentionally interrupted for users and they must take steps to resubscribe within the app, from Settings on iPhone and iPad, or in the App Store on Mac,\u201d the company explained in its announcement on Monday.<\/p>\nHowever, the flip side of this argument is that those same customers who would have missed the consent notification will likely be the same ones who would now miss the notification informing them their subscription will be increasing in price. There\u2019s also an argument here that this change could enable unscrupulous developers and scammers to better profit from their victims if Apple doesn’t carefully enforce the program rules.<\/p>\nCurrently, those state that developers can\u2019t increase prices more than once per year. The increase also can\u2019t exceed 50% of the subscription price, and the difference in price can\u2019t exceed $5 USD per period for non-annual subscriptions or $50 USD for annual subscriptions.<\/p>\nWeekly News<\/h1>\nPlatforms: Apple<\/h3>\n\nApple"https:\/\/9to5mac.com\/2022\/05\/19\/ios-15-6-beta-1-available-public-beta-testers\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">released<\/a> the first public betas of iOS 15.6,<\/strong>\u00a0iPadOS 15.6, tvOS 15.6,"https:\/\/www.imore.com\/how-download-watchos-8-public-beta\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">watchOS 8.7<\/a> and macOS 12.5. Now"https:\/\/9to5mac.com\/2022\/05\/18\/watchos-8-7-and-tvos-15-6-betas-join-homepod-software\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">included<\/a> in the beta lineup is HomePod Software 15.6.<\/li>\nApple also released iOS 15.5 to the public,<\/strong> which included a"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/16\/ios-15-5-apple-cash-update-send-request-money-wallet\/\">new way to request and send money<\/a> from their Apple Cash card through the Wallet app, as well as a\u00a0slew of\u00a0"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/16\/apple-podcasts-gains-storage-clean-up-tools-support-for-annual-subscriptions-and-a-new-distribution-system\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">new features for the Apple Podcasts app<\/a>, and"https:\/\/appleinsider.com\/articles\/22\/05\/17\/everything-new-in-ios-155-for-iphone?utm_medium=rss\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">other features.<\/a><\/li>\nThe latest Swift Playgrounds update (ver. 4.1)<\/strong>"https:\/\/appleinsider.com\/articles\/22\/05\/17\/swift-playgrounds-update-adds-app-store-connect-integration-for-macos-users?utm_medium=rss\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">added<\/a> App Store Connect integration for macOS users.<\/li>\nApple"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/apple-ad-data-brokers-privacy\/\">targeted<\/a> data brokers in its latest ad<\/strong> that promotes iOS privacy features.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n"embed-youtube embed breakout embed--video\" style=\"text-align:center; display: block;\">"youtube-player\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/embed\/NOXK4EVFmJY?version=3&rel=1&showsearch=0&showinfo=1&iv_load_policy=1&fs=1&hl=en-US&autohide=2&wmode=transparent\" allowfullscreen=\"true\" style=\"border:0;\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts allow-same-origin allow-popups allow-presentation\"><\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\nPlatforms: Google<\/h3>\n\nGoogle Play"https:\/\/www.androidpolice.com\/google-blocking-paid-app-updates-belarus-russia\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">expanded<\/a> its app sanctions against Russia to include Belarus.<\/strong>\u00a0The company will block the download of paid apps and updates to paid apps in both Russia and Belarus, it said in an update to its"https:\/\/support.google.com\/googleplay\/android-developer\/answer\/11950272?hl=en&ref_topic=3452890\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">help article<\/a> on the matter.<\/li>\nAlongside its announcement of its new Fire 7 tablet, Amazon"https:\/\/www.aftvnews.com\/amazon-will-debut-fire-os-8-based-on-android-11-next-month\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">also revealed<\/a> that its upcoming Fire OS 8,<\/strong> its own Android-based OS, will launch in June.<\/li>\nAn update to the Google System Update changelog<\/strong> again"https:\/\/www.androidpolice.com\/google-play-services-update-set-persistent-launcher-childs-device\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">indicates that Google’s Family Link software<\/a> will allow parents to set a persistent launcher on their child’s supervised device. This would make it so that a child couldn’t change the phone’s launcher to do anything other than what’s approved. The feature hasn’t been publicly announced.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nE-commerce and Food Delivery<\/h3>\n\nUber"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/19\/uber-grocery-outlet-pilot-on-demand-scheduled-grocery-delivery\/\">announced<\/a> a partnership with Grocery Outlet to pilot on-demand and scheduled grocery delivery.<\/strong> Initially, users can shop at 72 Grocery Outlet stores in California, Oregon and Washington state via the Uber or Uber Eats app.<\/li>\nUber also announced a whole host of new features at its"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/16\/everything-uber-announced-at-its-global-product-event\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">global product event<\/a> earlier in the week.<\/strong> Here, Uber launched an \u201cUber Travel\u201d feature that helps riders pre-book rides to and from upcoming events, like flights or restaurant reservations. It also announced an Uber Charter service for booking party buses, passenger vans and coach buses; plus event vouchers, an EV and charging map, various new Uber Eats products and additional perks for its Uber One membership; and more.<\/li>\nSnapchat and eBay announce integrations.<\/strong> Snapchat users can"https:\/\/newsroom.snap.com\/ebay-creativekit\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">now share eBay listings<\/a> with their friends using the Snapchat Camera on Android and iOS.<\/li>\nYouTube teased new features that it claims will make it easier for viewers to discover and buy from brands.<\/strong>\u00a0One new feature will allow two creators to go live at the same time to co-host a single live shopping stream. This could effectively double the draw for the event, as each creator would bring their own fanbase to the stream. Another upcoming option is called “live redirects.” With this, creators are able to start a shopping livestream on their channel, then redirect their audience over to a brand\u2019s channel for fans to keep watching. This allows brands to tap into the power of the creator\u2019s platform and reach their fanbase, but then gives the brands themselves access to that audience \u2014 and the key metrics and analytics associated with their live event \u2014 directly on their own YouTube channel.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nFintech<\/h3>\n\nFTX US"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/19\/crypto-exchange-ftx-expands-into-stock-trading-retail-investors\/\">plans to launch<\/a> FTX Stocks, a zero-commission stock trading feature available through the FTX mobile app,<\/strong> rolling out in the U.S. in the “coming months.” The news is particularly notable given that billionaire FTX US founder Sam Bankman-Fried recently acquired a 7.6% stake in Robinhood.<\/li>\nRobinhood will launch a standalone app that"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2022\/05\/17\/robinhood-to-let-users-hold-their-own-crypto-and-nfts-as-start-up-reaches-for-growth-beyond-stock-trading.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">lets users hold their own cryptocurrencies and NFTs<\/a>,<\/strong> putting it in direct competition with Coinbase and startups like MetaMask or Rainbow. The move comes at a time when Robinhood’s stocks are off by more than 70% since its IPO.<\/li>\nCoinbase"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/coinbase-backtracks-hiring-plans-crypto-market-turmoil\/\">backtracked on its hiring plans<\/a>, citing the crypto market turmoil.<\/strong> The company had earlier planned to triple headcount this year, but is now reassessing its headcount needs.<\/li>\nCoinbase also said it would let a “small set” of users"https:\/\/www.coindesk.com\/business\/2022\/05\/16\/coinbase-expands-features-allowing-some-app-users-to-access-ethereum-based-dapps\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">access Ethereum-based decentralized apps<\/a> directly from its own app via the new dApp browser.<\/strong> The feature would allow users to purchase NFTs on OpenSea and Coinbase\u2019s NFT platform; trade on decentralized exchanges like Uniswap and SushiSwap; and borrow and lend through DeFi platforms like Curve and Compound.<\/li>\nPlaid, whose service powers a number of fintech aps,"https:\/\/www.protocol.com\/fintech\/plaid-identity-verification\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> announced two products<\/a> for ACH transfers,<\/strong>\u00a0including identity verification, putting it into competition with Stripe.<\/li>\nGreenlight, a $2.3 billion fintech focused on kids,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/greenlight-fintech-focused-on-kids-launches-cash-back-credit-card-for-parents-education-savings\/\">launched a credit card for parents.<\/a><\/strong> The Greenlight-branded card, offered through Mastercard, offers up to 3% unlimited cash back on all purchases and gives parents the option to automatically invest those cash rewards in stocks and ETFs. They also can choose to invest the cash in other ways through the Greenlight mobile app or transfer funds to their bank.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nSocial<\/h3>\n\nTikTok launched Branded Mission,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/tiktoks-ad-product-gives-creators-opportunities-partner-marketers-branded-content\/\">a new ad product<\/a> that lets advertisers crowdsource content from creators with at least 1,000 followers.<\/strong> Advertisers can launch branded campaigns by developing a brief and releasing it to the creator community, encouraging them to participate in Branded Missions. Eligible creators whose videos are selected by brands will then benefit from a cash payment and boosted traffic.<\/li>\nTikTok"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/tiktok-launches-its-first-creator-crediting-tool-to-help-video-creators-cite-their-inspiration\/\">launched its first creator crediting tool<\/a> to help video creators cite their inspiration for dances, jokes, sounds and other content.<\/strong> The tool allows a creator to pick a video that’s then automatically added to their own video’s caption, linking back to the original creator. The changes follow years of complaints that top TikTok stars were lifting choreography from smaller creators, often Black creators. The problem got so bad that last year, some Black creators went on strike, refusing to create new dance moves for a recently dropped Megan Thee Stallion single as a form of protest.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n"attachment_2320815\" style=\"width: 8010px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2320815\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2320815 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"8000\" height=\"4500\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg 8000w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 8000px) 100vw, 8000px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2320815\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> TikTok<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n\nTwitter"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/twitter-rolls-out-super-follows-only-spaces\/\">rolled out the ability<\/a> for creators to host Super Follows-only Spaces as a subscriber perk.<\/strong> Subscribers globally on iOS and Android will be able to join and request to speak in Super Follows-only Spaces. (Web users can only join and listen for now.) Users who aren\u2019t Super Following a creator can still see the Space but won\u2019t be able to access it unless they subscribe.<\/li>\nSnap"https:\/\/newsroom.snap.com\/new-snap-originals-may-2022\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">announced<\/a> its new Snap Originals shows,<\/strong> which were also recently previewed at a company event. The show features stars like Simone Biles, winner of 32 Olympic and World Championship medals; NAACP Image Award winner La\u2019Ron Hines; Dixie and Charli D\u2019Amelio; and others.<\/li>\nFacebook and Twitter"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/buffalo-shooting-footage-facebook-twitter-moderation\/\">struggled to contain<\/a> the Buffalo shooting video<\/strong> which was circulating across their platforms where it was being reported by end users. The New York AG also"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/buffalo-shooting-twitch-discord-4chan-8chan-ny-ag\/\">announced<\/a> plans to investigate Twitch, Discord and 4chan for their role in the mass shooting.<\/li>\nSnap-owned social maps app Zenly, used by 35 million people monthly,<\/strong>"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/social-maps-app-zenly-rolls-out-its-own-maps\/\">rolled out its own<\/a> mapping data and engine following last month’s redesign. The project was built using open source data from OpenStreetMap and acquired datasets from third parties. The maps feature 3D landmarks, animated effects, tiny cars, people, 3D trees and more. The new maps are live in Taipei, Tokyo, Paris, Los Angeles, New York and Seoul.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n"attachment_2320599\" style=\"width: 2110px\" class=\"wp-caption around 8% of its workforce, amid the market downturn.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nDating<\/h3>\n\nRegulatory filings indicated Tiger Global sold off its entire stake in Bumble,<\/strong> along with other apps like Airbnb and Didi, as well as ~80% of its stake in Robinhood during 2022’s tech stock sell-off,"https:\/\/www.ft.com\/content\/a41a3676-a84c-4c55-b74a-9bc407abe748\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">FT reported<\/a>.<\/li>\nMatch Group-owned Hinge"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/hinges-latest-feature-aims-to-help-users-spark-conversations-about-self-care\/\">introduced<\/a> a new feature aimed at helping users initiate conversations about self-care.<\/strong> The new Self-Care Prompts may include things like \u201cThe last time I cried happy tears was\u2026,\u201d \u201cMy friends ask me for advice about\u2026,\u201d \u201cTo me, relaxation is\u2026,\u201d \u201cI feel most supported when\u2026,\u201d \u201cA boundary of mine is\u2026,” and others.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nMessaging<\/h3>\n\nMeta"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/19\/whatsapp-ramps-up-revenue-with-global-launch-of-cloud-api-and-soon-a-paid-tier-for-its-business-app\/\">launched its free WhatsApp Cloud API<\/a>, aimed at SMBs, to all businesses worldwide <\/strong>after earlier beta testing. The API allows companies to build on top of WhatsApp to better serve their customers, but without the costs and longer integration time for the on-premise version. WhatsApp also said it would roll outpaid features for its WhatsApp Business app<\/strong> later this year, including things like the ability to manage chats across up to 10 devices. The company will also provide new customizable WhatsApp click-to-chat links that help businesses attract customers across their online presence, it said.<\/li>\nWhatsApp is also developing a feature that will allow users to stealthily exit group chats without informing the group,<\/strong> according to a leak from WABetaInfo. The feature was"https:\/\/wabetainfo.com\/whatsapp-is-working-on-silently-exit-groups\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">developed for the new Communities feature<\/a> rolling out slowly this year.<\/li>\nIndian users of the Google Messages app say"https:\/\/9to5google.com\/2022\/05\/17\/google-messages-rcs-ads-india\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">RCS is being abused<\/a> by businesses to spam users with ads,<\/strong>\u00a0with the frequency of the ads picking up over the past few months.<\/li>\nApple’s Communication Safety in Messages"https:\/\/9to5mac.com\/2022\/05\/16\/ios-15-5-communication-safety-in-messages\/#more-805790\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">expanded<\/a> to more countries<\/strong> with iOS 15.5, including Australia, Canada, New Zealand and the U.K.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nStreaming & Entertainment<\/h3>\n\nYouTube\u2019s player"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/youtubes-player-gains-new-features-including-most-replayed-video-chapters-single-loop-and-more\/\">gained new features<\/a>, including Most Replayed, Video Chapters for big-screen devices, Single Loop and more.<\/strong>\u00a0The company said it\u2019s adding a graph that people can use to easily locate and watch the most replayed parts of a video \u2014 something that could be particularly helpful for longer videos or those that haven\u2019t broken down their various sections using either timestamps or video chapters. It also rolled out Video Chapters to smart TVs and gaming consoles and an option to set a video on a looping mode.<\/li>\nApple Music"https:\/\/9to5mac.com\/2022\/05\/17\/apple-music-streaming-live\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">launched<\/a> Apple Music Live, a new recurring series that will livestream concerts from major artists, kicking off with a Harry Styles concert Friday at 9 PM ET<\/strong> alongside the release of his third album, “Harry’s House.” Encore streams will run at 12:00 PM ET on\u00a0 May 22 and 5 AM ET on May 26. Apple wouldn’t say if VOD streams would ever be available.<\/li>\nSpotify and Accenture teamed up in order to"https:\/\/newsroom.spotify.com\/2022-05-18\/spotify-and-accenture-collaborate-to-offer-spotify-premium-as-an-employee-perk\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">offer Spotify Premium as an employee perk<\/a> as part of a new offering called “Spotify for Work.”<\/strong> Accenture kicked off the deal by rolling out Spotify to its employees across Sweden, Latvia and Lithuania.<\/li>\nYouTube Music for Wear OS"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/youtube-music-wear-os-stream-content-wi-fi-and-lte\/\">was updated<\/a> to allow users to stream content over Wi-Fi and LTE.<\/strong>\u00a0The feature means users will be able to listen to favorite songs even if their phone isn’t nearby.<\/li>\nCharli XCX is"https:\/\/pitchfork.com\/news\/charli-xcx-to-play-metaverse-concert-on-roblox-platform\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">scheduled<\/a> to play a “metaverse” concert on Roblox on June 17, 2022, at 7 PM ET.<\/strong> The concert will follow a five-week virtual event comprising mini-games and other digital challenges.<\/li>\nThe Apple Podcasts"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/16\/apple-podcasts-gains-storage-clean-up-tools-support-for-annual-subscriptions-and-a-new-distribution-system\/\">app gained new<\/a> storage clean-up tools, support for annual subscriptions and a new distribution system.<\/strong>\u00a0The new Apple Podcasts Delegated Delivery system will soon allow creators to more easily distribute their podcasts directly to Apple Podcasts from third-party hosting providers, including Acast, ART19, Blubrry, Buzzsprout, Libsyn, Omny Studio and RSS.com. The clean-up tools, meanwhile, will come in handy for better controlling how many episodes are saved locally and give you a chance to bulk remove downloads for the first time, including on Mac.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nGaming<\/h3>\n\nFortnite"https:\/\/blogs.nvidia.com\/blog\/2022\/05\/19\/geforce-now-thursday-may-19\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">launched<\/a> to all iOS users via Nvidia’s GeForce Now cloud gaming service<\/strong> after a few months of closed beta trials. The launch means iPhone users have yet another workaround to play the popular game on their device, despite its ban from the App Store, following Fortnite’s launch on Microsoft’s Cloud Gaming service earlier this month.<\/li>\nA report from"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/technology\/exclusive-tiktok-plans-big-push-into-gaming-conducting-tests-vietnam-sources-2022-05-19\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Reuters<\/a> said TikTok was testing HTML5 games in Vietnam, but TikTok"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/19\/tiktok-is-gearing-up-for-games-including-interactive-minigames-for-tiktok-live\/\">told<\/a> TechCrunch that was inaccurate — no games were currently testing in that market.<\/strong> However, the company had previously"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/09\/tiktok-ventures-into-mobile-gaming-initially-in-partnership-with-zynga\/\">confirmed<\/a> it was engaged in further gaming partnership discussions after its Zynga deal was announced.<\/li>\nTechCrunch"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/19\/tiktok-is-gearing-up-for-games-including-interactive-minigames-for-tiktok-live\/\">also reported and confirmed<\/a> a separate effort focused on bringing interactive minigames — like “Draw & Guess” — to the TikTok LIVE platform.<\/strong><\/li>\nNiantic\u2019s Pok\u00e9mon GO"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/19\/pokemon-go-amazon-prime-gaming-bonus\/\">partnered<\/a> with"https:\/\/gaming.amazon.com\/loot\/pokemongo\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Amazon Prime Gaming<\/a> and Prime Student to offer exclusive bonus item bundles every two weeks to Prime members.<\/strong> Users can log in to Prime and get a code, which they can redeem on Niantic\u2019s rewards page. The items will then appear in the game.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nSecurity & Privacy<\/h3>\n\nBrave’s iOS web browser was updated"https:\/\/brave.com\/1.38-release-ios\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">with a new Privacy Hub feature<\/a> <\/strong>that offers users more visibility on exactly what Brave blocked, and how Brave protects your personal information online. It does so by showing a rolling update of how many trackers Brave blocked on a specific site, or in a given time span. The hub also offers education about trackers and privacy threats.<\/li>\nApple"https:\/\/9to5mac.com\/2022\/05\/16\/apple-patches-27-security-flaws-ios-15-5\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">patched<\/a> almost 30 security flaws with iOS 15.5,<\/strong> as well as over 50 fixes for macOS 12.4.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nFunding and M&A<\/h1>\n\ud83d\udcb0 Pintarnya, a startup building a super app for Indonesia\u2019s blue-collar workers,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/pintarnya-is-building-a-super-app-for-indonesias-blue-collar-workers\/\">raised $6.3 million<\/a> in seed funding<\/strong> led by Sequoia Capital India and General Catalyst. The funding includes a $100,000 grant from Sequoia Spark, a program for women founders. The app offers verified job postings and financial services, like loans, for blue-collar workers.<\/p>\n\ud83d\udcb0 Instant delivery app Gopuff, valued at $15 billion,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/gopuff-the-instant-delivery-upstart-taps-ex-disney-head-bob-iger-as-its-newest-investor-and-advisor\/\">announced<\/a> a new advisor and investor: Bob Iger, the former CEO and chairman of The Walt Disney Company.<\/strong> The company wouldn’t say if the investment was coming as a separate investment, or as part of a $1 billion round (in debt and equity) that the company is in the process of closing.<\/p>\n\ud83d\udcb0 Instabug, a startup that helps mobile developers monitor, identify and fix bugs within apps,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/instabug-lands-46m-to-help-keep-your-apps-from-crashing\/\">raised $46 million<\/a> in Series B funding led by Insight Partners.<\/strong> The company said its ARR doubled in 2021 and the number of enterprise customers grew 10x, as it added new clients like DoorDash, Verizon, Qualtrics, Porsche and Gojek. Last year, its software sat within 2.7 billion mobile devices, processed 110 billion mobile sessions (up at least 20x from 2020) and helped customers resolve 4.2 billion issues, it said.<\/p>\n\ud83d\udcb0 Unit, a banking-as-a-service startup that allows developers to easily build new fintech apps,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/banking-as-a-service-startup-unit-closes-on-100m-at-a-1-2b-valuation\/\">raised $100 million<\/a> in Series C funding led by Insight Partners, at a $1.2 billion valuation.<\/strong> Unit said its transaction volume grew 7x over the past six months and has crossed an annualized transaction volume of $2.6 billion. Every week, the new TC podcast will dive into the biggest stories in tech, as told by the writers who penned them. If there’s one thing TC is great at, it’s rolling with the punches and improvising on the fly, and we did that with on-location and remote recording, bringing you highlights from the biggest news of the week alongside in-depth interviews with TC’s own Kirsten Korosec and Taylor Hatmaker.<\/p>\nBe sure to subscribe, and leave us a 5-star review with your feedback. TechCrunch Podcast","slug":"the-techcrunch-podcast","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576595654"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576595654"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576595654"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576595654"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576595654"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":67677,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/ufo\/","name":"UFO","slug":"ufo","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/67677"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=67677"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=67677"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=67677"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=67677"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2322082,"date":"2022-05-21T07:00:13","date_gmt":"2022-05-21T14:00:13","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2322082"},"modified":"2022-05-20T10:02:21","modified_gmt":"2022-05-20T17:02:21","slug":"a-weaker-economy-wont-solve-the-tech-talent-crunch-overnight","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/21\/a-weaker-economy-wont-solve-the-tech-talent-crunch-overnight\/","title":{"rendered":"A weaker economy won\u2019t solve the tech talent crunch overnight"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">"featured__span-first-words\">As bad economic<\/span> news piles up seemingly"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/16\/how-quickly-are-startup-layoffs-accelerating\/\">on a daily basis<\/a>, we don\u2019t know what"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2022\/04\/28\/us-q1-gdp-growth.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the future holds<\/a> except that change is on the way. Although we are seeing layoffs and"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/13\/startup-tech-layoff-and-hiring-freeze-in-may\/\">hiring freezes<\/a> at some companies, it doesn\u2019t necessarily mean the talent crunch will immediately abate.<\/p>\nThere will likely be some lag before we start to see"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/recruit-retain-resign-re-skill-repeat\/\">the tight job market<\/a> we\u2019ve experienced for the last couple of years begin to loosen. Even then, there are certain fields like engineering, data science and"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/10\/5-ways-to-attract-top-cybersecurity-talent-in-a-tight-labor-market\/\">cybersecurity<\/a>, where tech companies large and small could still struggle to find talent no matter what the macroeconomic conditions look like.<\/p>\nOver the last month, we have seen an increase in the number of"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/06\/startup-tech-layoffs-in-may\/\">startup layoff announcements<\/a> at companies like Cameo, On Deck and Robinhood. Meanwhile, big companies like Netflix, Meta and Uber have announced hiring freezes, with the consumer streaming service throwing"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/netflix-lays-off-150-staffers-citing-slowing-revenue-growth\/\">some layoffs<\/a> into the mix as well.<\/p>\nDespite this onslaught of bad news, for now, most startup founders, investors and HR pros don\u2019t see the job market magically improving for hiring departments, at least in the near term. That means the folks in charge of hiring are still going to have to shake the bushes for talent.<\/p>\nMatt Hoffman, partner and head of talent at VC firm M13 and a former HR pro, said for a lot of people, the desire to be a part of something and help it grow is in some ways a stronger motivator than perks and pay. That\u2019s good news for startups looking for talent.<\/p>\n“I’ve always believed that people don’t join a company just for the economic benefits. They join for the opportunity to have an impact and to grow. And so in a lot of cases, it may be a more opportune time to take a chance in an early-stage company because you can focus on that long-term horizon, and you can get that opportunity to grow and have an impact,\u201d Hoffman told me.<\/p>\nFor employees, he said there will still be opportunities at good companies in any economic conditions, but attracting talent always comes down to creating a good place to work.<\/p>\n“Even in the tightest of economic environments \u2014 and we\u2019re not there yet \u2014 there\u2019s always going to be high demand for the best talent. Always. So the things that you need to do to attract, engage and retain these employees does not change,” he said.

/battlefield-companies?tags=26402"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=26402"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=26402"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576710221,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/m13\/","name":"M13","slug":"m13","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576710221"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576710221"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576710221"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576710221"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576710221"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[{"id":576796357,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/techcrunchplus\/work\/","name":"Work","slug":"work","taxonomy":"tc_ec_category","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_ec_category\/576796357"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_ec_category"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/tc_ec_category"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tc_ec_category=576796357"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[]]}},{"id":2322890,"date":"2022-05-20T18:02:49","date_gmt":"2022-05-21T01:02:49","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2322890"},"modified":"2022-05-21T11:03:30","modified_gmt":"2022-05-21T18:03:30","slug":"pear-now-nearly-10-years-old-and-with-numerous-hits-just-closed-its-biggest-fund-by-far","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/20\/pear-now-nearly-10-years-old-and-with-numerous-hits-just-closed-its-biggest-fund-by-far\/","title":{"rendered":"Pear, now nearly 10 years old and with numerous hits, looks to close its biggest fund by far"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Pear, a Palo Alto, Ca.-based venture firm that we’ve been tracking since its outset in 2012, looks to be raising a fourth fund that’s targeting $410 million in capital commitments, shows a new"https:\/\/www.sec.gov\/Archives\/edgar\/data\/0001927410\/000192741022000001\/xslFormDX01\/primary_doc.xml\">SEC filing<\/a>.<\/p>\nIt would be a big step up from Pear’s first three funds, which closed progressively with $50 million in 2013, $75 million in 2016, and $160 million in capital commitments in 2019, including from a longtime limited partner, the University of Chicago.<\/p>\nReached for comment, cofounder Pejman Nozad emailed back, “I can’t comment!”<\/p>\nNozad and cofounder Mar Hershenson have long been first-stop for prominent early-stage investors that are looking to fund nascent teams, given the firm has been among the earliest backers in a notable number of companies that have gone to raise ever-bigger rounds and higher valuations, including the now publicly traded companies DoorDash and Guardant Health.<\/p>\nOther startups to attract capital from Pear before nearly any other firm was aware of their existence include the deep-linking startup Branch, which closed on"https:\/\/www.prnewswire.com\/news-releases\/branch-raises-300-million-at-4-billion-valuation-to-open-mobile-ecosystem-and-provide-solution-to-walled-gardens-301479684.html\">$300 million<\/a> in funding in February at a $4 billion valuation; Gusto, valued at $9.5 billion last summer when it raised"https:\/\/www.forbes.com\/sites\/davidjeans\/2021\/08\/10\/gusto-10-billion-ipo-hr-software\/?sh=6e04e89a6c92\">$175 million<\/a> in funding; and Aurora Solar, a firm that provides software services for the solar industry and was valued at $4 billion in February when it closed a"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2022-02-28\/aurora-solar-gets-4-billion-valuation-on-backing-led-by-coatue?sref=gni836kR\">$200 million<\/a> round.<\/p>\nLike other firms, Pear is likely to see the valuations of its still-private portfolio companies slide downward — possibly by a lot — depending on how long this correction lasts.<\/p>\nHershenson, who joined TechCrunch for a mobility-focused event this week, noted on stage that startups are in for a bumpy ride, given how frothy the market had grown.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nAsked if the"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/for-tech-startups-the-party-is-over-11652710330?mod=tech_lead_pos5\">startup party is over<\/a>, Hershenson answered: “Maybe for a little while it’s over . . .The problem is that the market was priced too high in 2021, and we’re all adjusting to that price change, and that changes how companies raise money.<\/p>\n“Everybody knows that the stock market is down a lot,” she’d said. “Software stocks are down in some cases 80%. [Meanwhile] if you’re a private company, and you were very lucky and you raised money in 2021, you may have gotten a multiple of 100x on your ARR. Today, those multiples are 10x or 20x. That means that if your company was $2 billion [at the time of your fundraise], your company is [now] worth $200 million.:<\/p>\nEven with a steep reset in prices, however, Pear’s success to date is undeniable. It’s also unlikely.<\/p>\nNozad, very famously, was earlier a rug dealer who insisted on toting rugs to his clients’ homes, where during the course of long conversations, they would learn about the rug and he would learn about their business. He eventually became a scout for his boss, and a trusted friend to some very powerful people.<\/p>\n\u201cHe has a good sniffer, and I trust the guy,\u201d\u00a0 Sequoia\u2019s Doug Leone"https:\/\/www.forbes.com\/sites\/victoriabarret\/2012\/03\/21\/silicon-valleys-hottest-vc-is-a-rug-dealer\/?sh=3dfe6dbb31d5\">told Forbes<\/a> back in 2012. \u201cHe\u2019s like me, from the earth.\u201d Sequoia has, in fact, backed a number of companies that Pear has funded, including Guardant Health and DoorDash.<\/p>\nMeanwhile, his partner, Mar Hershenson, was also very much an outlier when the two struck out on their own. Despite founding several companies previously — one of which Nozad backed — and though she holds an M.S. and Ph.D. degrees in electrical engineering from Stanford University, she is a native of Spain and even more unusual in VC circles a decade ago, she is a woman who had not previously cut her teeth at someone else’s venture firm.<\/p>\nThat may not seem very notable today but in 2012, it put Hershenson in rare company.<\/p>\nAs for the team’s newest bets, Pear hosted an invite-only demo day earlier this week, coverage of which we’ll have for readers soon. (Unlike Y Combinator, the outfit holds a demo day each year for a comparatively limited number of companies — typically around 10.)<\/p>\nIn the meantime, some of its other recent checks have gone to Sudozi, a two-year-old Austin, Tex., startup that provides a SaaS platform to help enterprises improve their money management capabilities and that just this month announced a"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2022\/05\/12\/sudozi-nabs-4-3m-to-simplify-money-management-for-enterprises\/\">$4.3 million<\/a> seed round led by Pear.<\/p>\nPear also recently wrote a follow-on check to Osmind, a two-year-old, Bay Area-based startup that makes software to chart and update patient information and documents, with a focus on mental health. The outfit raised"https:\/\/www.fastcompany.com\/90750411\/osmind-raises-40-million-to-expand-electronic-records-for-mental-health\">$40 million<\/a> in Series B funding led by DFJ Growth, an announcement it also made earlier this month.<\/p>\nCorrection: This story originally reported that Pear’s newest fund is closed; we’ve updated the story to reflect that the fund is still being raised.<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Pear, a Palo Alto, Ca.-based venture firm that we’ve been tracking since its outset in 2012, looks to be raising a fourth fund that’s targeting $410 million in capital commitments, shows a new SEC filing. It would be a big step up from Pear’s first three funds, which closed progressively with $50 million in 2013, week in TechCrunch podcasts: The new TC Pod, Chain Reaction, Found, Equity and The TechCrunch Live Podcast"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">TechCrunch is more than just a site with words. We’re also building a growing stable of podcasts focused on the most critical topics relating to the startup and venture capital worlds. To help you find the right show for your interests, we’ve compiled our audio output from the week.<\/p>\nEmbedded below is the latest from"https:\/\/podcasts.apple.com\/us\/podcast\/chain-reaction\/id1616008890\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Chain Reaction<\/a>, our new and stellar crypto-focused podcast hosted by"https:\/\/twitter.com\/lucasmtny\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Lucas<\/a> and"https:\/\/twitter.com\/AnitaRamaswamy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Anita<\/a>. You will also find"https:\/\/podcasts.apple.com\/us\/podcast\/found\/id1561051074\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Found<\/a>, a long-form bit of work that goes deep on the real saga of company formation from"https:\/\/twitter.com\/jordanrcrook?lang=en\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Jordan<\/a> and"https:\/\/twitter.com\/etherington\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Darrell<\/a>. There’s an audio-only version of"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/techcrunchlive\/\">TechCrunch Live<\/a> hosted by"https:\/\/twitter.com\/mjburnsy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Matt<\/a> that features founders and investors discussing successful pitch decks. Finally, there’s"https:\/\/podcasts.apple.com\/us\/podcast\/equity\/id1215439780\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Equity<\/a>, TechCrunch’s long-running, Webby-award-winning podcast focused on venture capital and the latest startup news, hosted by"http:\/\/twitter.com\/nmasc_\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Natasha<\/a>,"http:\/\/twitter.com\/bayareawriter\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Mary Ann<\/a> and"http:\/\/twitter.com\/alex\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Alex<\/a>.<\/em><\/p>\nAnd if you are more into the written over the spoken word, well"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/newsletters\">we have newsletters<\/a> on the above topics as well.<\/p>\n"gradient-text gradient-text--green-gradient\">TechCrunch Podcast<\/span><\/h2>\nEpisode 1: TechCrunch reporters Taylor Hatmaker and Kirsten Korosec join host Darrell Etherington<\/strong><\/p>\n"https:\/\/player.simplecast.com\/3cffe965-f16a-4584-b69d-87e67f0d751f?dark=false\" width=\"100%\" height=\"200px\" frameborder=\"no\" scrolling=\"no\" seamless=\"\"><\/iframe><\/p>\nWelcome to the very first episode of The TechCrunch Podcast! Every week, the new TC podcast will dive into the biggest stories in tech, as told by the writers who penned them. We’ve been developing and iterating on the concept for many months now, so we’re thrilled to finally be able to deliver our first ever full episode, which you can get by subscribing"https:\/\/podcasts.apple.com\/us\/podcast\/the-techcrunch-podcast\/id1624500693\">here on Apple Podcasts<\/a> or"https:\/\/open.spotify.com\/show\/7gaqQOeUbC6hfMkVA5fih3?si=b30642b7f1e54ea5\">Spotify<\/a>.<\/p>\nOur first ever show is typical for TechCrunch, since it was recorded mostly on the road at one of our fantastic yearly events \u2013"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-mobility-2022\/\">TechCrunch Mobility 2022<\/a>! If there’s one thing TC is great at, it’s rolling with the punches and improvising on the fly, and we did that with on-location and remote recording, bringing you highlights from the biggest news of the week alongside in-depth interviews with TC’s own Kirsten Korosec and Taylor Hatmaker.<\/p>\nBe sure to subscribe, and leave us a 5-star review with your feedback. We’ll be delivering the TechCrunch Podcast weekly, with fresh interviews from the writers closest to the biggest stories of the week, as well as a roundup of what you need to know for what went down in the wide world of tech.<\/p>\n\/>\n"gradient-text gradient-text--green-gradient\">Chain Reaction<\/span><\/h2>\nEpisode 6: Lightspeed\u2019s web3 guru on consumer crypto startups and the metaverse (with Mercedes Bent)<\/strong><\/p>\n"https:\/\/player.simplecast.com\/6c95a13b-acfb-478d-9707-30750d5d461f?dark=false\" width=\"100%\" height=\"200px\" frameborder=\"no\" scrolling=\"no\" seamless=\"\"><\/iframe><\/p>\nWelcome back, this week Lucas and Anita discuss the continued fallout from the broader market crash and how life is going for crypto giants on the public markets. We chat about FTX\u2019s 30-year-old billionaire CEO buying up a big chunk of Robinhood, which is pumping the gas on crypto even as the market cools. We also discuss trouble at Coinbase and the continued fallout from the collapse of Terra.<\/p>\nIn their interview this week, Lucas and Anita chat with Mercedes Bent. Bent is a venture capitalist at Lightspeed Venture Partners where she places bets on consumer products in cryptoland. Before joining Lightspeed, Bent spent some time in the VR world, so we picked her brain on where crypto fits into this metaverse future everyone is clamoring about.<\/p>\nSubscribe to the Chain Reaction newsletter to dive deeper:"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/newsletters\">https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/newsletters<\/a><\/p>\n\/>\n"gradient-text gradient-text--green-gradient\">Found<\/span><\/h2>\nEpisode 57: Justin Intal, Forage<\/strong><\/p>\n"https:\/\/player.simplecast.com\/9824a26d-62ba-4b17-9c8a-6f53fc520ee5?dark=false\" width=\"100%\" height=\"200px\" frameborder=\"no\" scrolling=\"no\" seamless=\"\"><\/iframe><\/p>\nJustin Intal from Forage joined the Found crew live. He talks about how profound struggles in her personal life motivated him to create a way for online grocers to accept EBT and SNAP benefits.
