Week in Apps: Snapchat policy checkup, more Twitter deal drama, TikTok games"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Welcome back to This Week in Apps,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/this-week-in-apps\/\">the weekly TechCrunch series<\/a> that recaps the latest in mobile OS news, mobile applications and the overall app economy.<\/p>\nThe app industry continues to grow, with"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/07\/app-stores-to-see-record-consumer-spend-of-133-billion-in-2021-143-6-billion-new-app-installs\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">a record<\/a> number of downloads and consumer spending across both the iOS and Google Play stores combined in 2021, according to the"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/07\/app-stores-to-see-record-consumer-spend-of-133-billion-in-2021-143-6-billion-new-app-installs\/\">latest<\/a> year-end"https:\/\/www.appannie.com\/en\/insights\/market-data\/2021-end-year-mobile-apps-recap\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reports<\/a>. App Annie says global spending across iOS and Google Play is up to $135 billion in 2021, and that figure will likely be higher when its annual report, including third-party app stores in China, is released next year. Consumers also downloaded 10 billion more apps in 2021 than in 2020, reaching nearly 140 billion in new installs, it found.<\/p>\nApps aren\u2019t just a way to pass idle hours \u2014 they\u2019re also a big business. In 2019, mobile-first companies had a"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/15\/app-stores-saw-record-204-billion-app-downloads-in-2019-consumer-spend-of-120-billion\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">combined<\/a> $544 billion valuation, 6.5x higher than those without a mobile focus. In 2020, investors"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/13\/app-stores-saw-record-218-billion-downloads-in-2020-consumer-spend-of-143-billion\/\">poured<\/a> $73 billion in capital into mobile companies \u2014 a figure that was up 27% year-over-year.<\/p>\nThis Week in Apps offers a way to keep up with this fast-moving industry in one place with the latest from the world of apps, including news, updates, startup fundings, mergers and acquisitions, and much more.<\/p>\nDo you want This Week in Apps in your inbox every Saturday? Sign up here:"http:\/\/techcrunch.com\/newsletters\">techcrunch.com\/newsletters<\/a><\/strong><\/em><\/p>\nTop Stories<\/h1>\nApps celebrate Global Accessibility Awareness Day<\/h3>\nThis past Thursday, May 19, 2022, marked the 11th Global Accessibility Awareness Day (GAAD), which is a day focused on raising awareness about digital access and inclusion for the more than 1 billion people who live with disabilities or impairments. A number of app makers and tech companies took part in GAAD this year to either highlight or announce new features designed to better meet the needs of those with vision impairment, hearing loss and other disabilities.<\/p>\nInstagram’s"https:\/\/about.instagram.com\/micro_site\/url\/?click_from_context_menu=true&country=US&destination=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.instagram.com%2Fcreators%2F&event_type=click&last_nav_impression_id=1CdGKXYlYDe4E0lHE&max_percent_page_viewed=64&max_viewport_height_px=650&max_viewport_width_px=1440&orig_request_uri=https%3A%2F%2Fabout.instagram.com%2Fblog%2Ftips-and-tricks%2Fadvancing-accessibility-on-instagram%2F&region=noam&scrolled=true&session_id=0CY7cymmK4zmFenWR&site=instagram_about\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">@creators account<\/a> shared information with its community about how and why to use accessibility features, like alt-text and auto-generated captions to create a better experience for your audience. The company"https:\/\/about.instagram.com\/blog\/tips-and-tricks\/advancing-accessibility-on-instagram\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">also noted other developments<\/a> it had rolled out, like dark mode, screen reader improvements, improved automatic and custom alternative text options for people with vision impairments, caption stickers for Reels and Stories, and more. The company also said it has started rolling out closed caption features to improve the Instagram experience for the deaf and hard of hearing communities. These changes help to improve the experience for everyone, however, as Instagram said one-third of video plays on Instagram are with the sound off. In March, Instagram made"u_0_c_aa\" class=\"_8ow9 _9gii\" href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/instagram\/status\/1498710216585613314\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">"_8-vl _8-vp\">"_95iu _8iqw\">auto-generated captions the default<\/span><\/span><\/a> for creators, which are supported globally across iOS and Android.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nGoogle shared its approach to both hiring people with disabilities and building products to meet their needs. For example, it highlighted projects like"https:\/\/blog.google\/outreach-initiatives\/accessibility\/project-relate\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-onclick=\"{"event":"page interaction","category":"in-article links","action":"link click","label":"https:\/\/blog.google\/outreach-initiatives\/accessibility\/project-relate\/"}\">Project Relate<\/a>, a communication tool for people with speech impairments; the update to"https:\/\/blog.google\/products\/android\/all-new-talkback\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-onclick=\"{"event":"page interaction","category":"in-article links","action":"link click","label":"https:\/\/blog.google\/products\/android\/all-new-talkback\/"}\">\u00a0TalkBack<\/a>, Android\u2019s built-in screen reader; and the"https:\/\/blog.google\/products\/chromebooks\/accessibility-features\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-onclick=\"{"event":"page interaction","category":"in-article links","action":"link click","label":"https:\/\/blog.google\/products\/chromebooks\/accessibility-features\/"}\">improved Select-to-Speak<\/a> Chromebook tool; a multi-pin feature for Google Meet, which allows users to pin multiple tiles, like a presenter’s screen and interpreter’s screen. The company also noted all its English-language YouTube Originals content from the past year \u2014 and moving forward \u2014 will now have English audio descriptions available globally.<\/p>\nApple, meanwhile, participated in GAAD with a number of"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/apple-adds-live-captions-to-iphone-and-mac-plus-more-accessibility-upgrades-to-come\/\">announcements<\/a> about"https:\/\/www.apple.com\/newsroom\/2022\/05\/apple-previews-innovative-accessibility-features\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">new accessibility features<\/a> for iPhone, Apple Watch and Mac.<\/p>\nThese included a universal Live Captions feature, improved visual and auditory detection modes and iOS access to WatchOS apps. Live Captions will be able to transcribe any audio content, like FaceTime calls, video conferencing apps and streaming video, as well as in-person conversations, all in English to start.<\/p>\n"attachment_2322399\" style=\"width: 1970px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2322399\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2322399 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1960\" height=\"1102\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg 1960w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg?resize=680,382 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Apple-Accessibility-OS-features-2022-hero_big.jpg.large_2x.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1960px) 100vw, 1960px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2322399\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Apple<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nApple’s Sound Recognition feature will be able to be programmed to recognize sounds unique to a person’s own home, like their doorbell or appliances. The Magnifier app will add a new ML and lidar-powered Door Detection feature within a new Detection Mode section. This will help users locate a door, understand how far they are from it and describe door attributes. Apple Maps will offer sound and haptics feedback for VoiceOver users. And Apple Watch will help users control Apple Watch remotely from their paired iPhone with Apple Watch Mirroring. It also gains new Quick Action like a double-pinch gesture to answer or end a phone call, dismiss a notification, take a photo, play or pause media in the Now Playing app, and start, pause or resume a workout.<\/p>\nSnap’s platform policies for third-party apps aren’t yet fully enforced<\/h3>\n"attachment_2167646\" style=\"width: 3210px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2167646\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2167646 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/snapchat-speed-blur.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"3200\" height=\"1800\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/snapchat-speed-blur.jpg 3200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/snapchat-speed-blur.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/snapchat-speed-blur.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/snapchat-speed-blur.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/snapchat-speed-blur.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/snapchat-speed-blur.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/snapchat-speed-blur.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/snapchat-speed-blur.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 3200px) 100vw, 3200px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2167646\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nA handful of Snap Kit platform developers"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/snapchats-stricter-policies-for-anonymous-apps-and-friend-finders-arent-yet-fully-enforced\/\">have not yet complied<\/a> with the new guidelines around anonymous messaging and friend-finding apps"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/following-suicides-and-lawsuits-snapchat-restricts-apps-building-on-its-platform-with-new-policies\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">announced in March<\/a>. The Snapchat maker revamped its developer platform policies on March 17, 2022, to ban anonymous apps and require developers to build friend-finding apps to limit access to users 18 or older. The policy changes were effective immediately and existing developers were given 30 days to come into compliance \u2014 a date that would have passed last month.<\/p>\nIt is now mid-May and some developers of the newly banned and restricted apps are not yet meeting Snap\u2019s new requirements.<\/p>\nSnap confirmed to TechCrunch a small number of apps were given extensions, including anonymous apps LMK and Send It. But others seemed to be working around Snap’s ban with their friend-finding apps marketed to users ages 12+, instead of the now required 18+. They got away with this by not actually using the SDK — something impossible to tell from their App Store marketing and screenshots which imply they’re directly integrated with Snap’s features. Another app had flown under the radar, continuing to operate in violation of the rules unless TechCrunch pointed it out, resulting in a belated ban. This lack of clarity on which apps are platform apps, and which are only pretending to be, could complicate things for Snap, which is engaged in litigation over bullying-related suicides. And like all social media, the company could be under new U.S. regulation related to child safety matters in the future, as well.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Bd2UjCgxsR\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/snapchats-stricter-policies-for-anonymous-apps-and-friend-finders-arent-yet-fully-enforced\/\">Snapchat’s stricter policies for anonymous apps and friend finders aren’t yet fully enforced<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Snapchat’s stricter policies for anonymous apps and friend finders aren’t yet fully enforced” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/snapchats-stricter-policies-for-anonymous-apps-and-friend-finders-arent-yet-fully-enforced\/embed\/#?secret=e39VRJvFjG#?secret=Bd2UjCgxsR\" data-secret=\"Bd2UjCgxsR\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\nTwitter deal still a go… for now<\/h3>\nFirst,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/13\/elon-musk-twitter-deal-on-hold-spam\/\">Elon Musk tweeted<\/a> that the Twitter deal was “temporarily on hold” until Twitter could prove the percentage of spambots on its platform was actually less than 5%, as it reports. This Tuesday, he"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/elon-musk-twitter-spam\/\">reiterated<\/a> the deal would not move forward until Twitter would show him proof of this <5% figure. Twitter was having none of it, though. The company filed a"https:\/\/www.sec.gov\/Archives\/edgar\/data\/0001418091\/000119312522152250\/d283119dprem14a.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">\u00a0proxy statement<\/a>, saying it’s committed to the deal as agreed and is ready to close “as promptly as possible.”<\/p>\nIf Musk’s move was an"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/opinion\/articles\/2022-05-17\/elon-musk-does-not-care-about-spam-bots?sref=gni836kR\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">attempt to renegotiate the price<\/a>, it didn’t seem to be working. Twitter’s top lawyer and head of policy, Vijaya Gadde, told staff at an all-hands meeting there’s “no such thing as a deal being on hold,” reported"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2022-05-19\/twitter-deal-is-proceeding-not-on-hold-executives-tell-staff?sref=gni836kR\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bloomberg<\/a>. Twitter execs also suggested that it could try to enforce the deal terms in court, if need be, but said that would be “pretty rare” for such a thing to occur. (Not that this Twitter deal is proceeding normally though!) There’s still some speculation that Musk is looking to fully back out and will find a way to do so, billion-dollar breakup fee notwithstanding. In the meantime, the bankers are"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2022-05-18\/as-musk-tweets-advisers-plug-away-to-keep-twitter-deal-on-track\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">still preparing the paperwork<\/a> and execs are"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2022-05-17\/twitter-loses-three-more-senior-employees-ahead-of-musk-takeover?sref=gni836kR\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">still leaving<\/a>. This week, it was Twitter Service VP Katrina Lane, head of data science Max Schmeiser and VP of product management Ilya Brown — all of whom chose to leave on their own.<\/p>\nApple\u2019s new rules let apps raise subscription prices automatically<\/h3>\n"attachment_2133289\" style=\"width: 3210px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2133289\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2133289 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"3200\" height=\"1800\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg 3200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/04\/app-store-2021-pattern.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 3200px) 100vw, 3200px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2133289\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nAlongside the launch of the iOS 15.5 update, Apple introduced a new set of rules to govern auto-renewing subscriptions on the App Store. Now, instead of asking users to agree to any subscription price increases, developers will be able to roll out a price increase with the user\u2019s explicit consent. The feature allows developers to simply inform customers they\u2019ll be charged more, but not require the customer to opt-in to the higher pricing.<\/p>\n"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/05\/apple-pilot-tests-feature-that-allows-developers-to-automatically-charge-users-for-subscription-price-increases\/\">We first broke the news that Apple was pilot testing this program<\/a> last month, when it appeared Disney+ subscription customers had simply been told their price was increasing but weren\u2019t asked for their consent. Apple then confirmed this was the result of a \u201cnew commerce feature\u201d it planned to launch soon, which it said would be \u201cgreat for both developers and users.\u201d<\/p>\nApple\u2019s position is that this could save customers the hassle of having their subscriptions automatically canceled just because they didn\u2019t see the notification or email that asked them to opt in to the price increase.<\/p>\n\u201cThis has led to some services being unintentionally interrupted for users and they must take steps to resubscribe within the app, from Settings on iPhone and iPad, or in the App Store on Mac,\u201d the company explained in its announcement on Monday.<\/p>\nHowever, the flip side of this argument is that those same customers who would have missed the consent notification will likely be the same ones who would now miss the notification informing them their subscription will be increasing in price. There\u2019s also an argument here that this change could enable unscrupulous developers and scammers to better profit from their victims if Apple doesn’t carefully enforce the program rules.<\/p>\nCurrently, those state that developers can\u2019t increase prices more than once per year. The increase also can\u2019t exceed 50% of the subscription price, and the difference in price can\u2019t exceed $5 USD per period for non-annual subscriptions or $50 USD for annual subscriptions.<\/p>\nWeekly News<\/h1>\nPlatforms: Apple<\/h3>\n\nApple"https:\/\/9to5mac.com\/2022\/05\/19\/ios-15-6-beta-1-available-public-beta-testers\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">released<\/a> the first public betas of iOS 15.6,<\/strong>\u00a0iPadOS 15.6, tvOS 15.6,"https:\/\/www.imore.com\/how-download-watchos-8-public-beta\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">watchOS 8.7<\/a> and macOS 12.5. The feature was"https:\/\/wabetainfo.com\/whatsapp-is-working-on-silently-exit-groups\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">developed for the new Communities feature<\/a> rolling out slowly this year.<\/li>\nIndian users of the Google Messages app say"https:\/\/9to5google.com\/2022\/05\/17\/google-messages-rcs-ads-india\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">RCS is being abused<\/a> by businesses to spam users with ads,<\/strong>\u00a0with the frequency of the ads picking up over the past few months.<\/li>\nApple’s Communication Safety in Messages"https:\/\/9to5mac.com\/2022\/05\/16\/ios-15-5-communication-safety-in-messages\/#more-805790\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">expanded<\/a> to more countries<\/strong> with iOS 15.5, including Australia, Canada, New Zealand and the U.K.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nStreaming & Entertainment<\/h3>\n\nYouTube\u2019s player"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/youtubes-player-gains-new-features-including-most-replayed-video-chapters-single-loop-and-more\/\">gained new features<\/a>, including Most Replayed, Video Chapters for big-screen devices, Single Loop and more.<\/strong>\u00a0The company said it\u2019s adding a graph that people can use to easily locate and watch the most replayed parts of a video \u2014 something that could be particularly helpful for longer videos or those that haven\u2019t broken down their various sections using either timestamps or video chapters. It also rolled out Video Chapters to smart TVs and gaming consoles and an option to set a video on a looping mode.<\/li>\nApple Music"https:\/\/9to5mac.com\/2022\/05\/17\/apple-music-streaming-live\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">launched<\/a> Apple Music Live, a new recurring series that will livestream concerts from major artists, kicking off with a Harry Styles concert Friday at 9 PM ET<\/strong> alongside the release of his third album, “Harry’s House.” Encore streams will run at 12:00 PM ET on\u00a0 May 22 and 5 AM ET on May 26. Apple wouldn’t say if VOD streams would ever be available.<\/li>\nSpotify and Accenture teamed up in order to"https:\/\/newsroom.spotify.com\/2022-05-18\/spotify-and-accenture-collaborate-to-offer-spotify-premium-as-an-employee-perk\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">offer Spotify Premium as an employee perk<\/a> as part of a new offering called “Spotify for Work.”<\/strong> Accenture kicked off the deal by rolling out Spotify to its employees across Sweden, Latvia and Lithuania.<\/li>\nYouTube Music for Wear OS"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/youtube-music-wear-os-stream-content-wi-fi-and-lte\/\">was updated<\/a> to allow users to stream content over Wi-Fi and LTE.<\/strong>\u00a0The feature means users will be able to listen to favorite songs even if their phone isn’t nearby.<\/li>\nCharli XCX is"https:\/\/pitchfork.com\/news\/charli-xcx-to-play-metaverse-concert-on-roblox-platform\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">scheduled<\/a> to play a “metaverse” concert on Roblox on June 17, 2022, at 7 PM ET.<\/strong> The concert will follow a five-week virtual event comprising mini-games and other digital challenges.<\/li>\nThe Apple Podcasts"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/16\/apple-podcasts-gains-storage-clean-up-tools-support-for-annual-subscriptions-and-a-new-distribution-system\/\">app gained new<\/a> storage clean-up tools, support for annual subscriptions and a new distribution system.<\/strong>\u00a0The new Apple Podcasts Delegated Delivery system will soon allow creators to more easily distribute their podcasts directly to Apple Podcasts from third-party hosting providers, including Acast, ART19, Blubrry, Buzzsprout, Libsyn, Omny Studio and RSS.com. The clean-up tools, meanwhile, will come in handy for better controlling how many episodes are saved locally and give you a chance to bulk remove downloads for the first time, including on Mac.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nGaming<\/h3>\n\nFortnite"https:\/\/blogs.nvidia.com\/blog\/2022\/05\/19\/geforce-now-thursday-may-19\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">launched<\/a> to all iOS users via Nvidia’s GeForce Now cloud gaming service<\/strong> after a few months of closed beta trials. The launch means iPhone users have yet another workaround to play the popular game on their device, despite its ban from the App Store, following Fortnite’s launch on Microsoft’s Cloud Gaming service earlier this month.<\/li>\nA report from"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/technology\/exclusive-tiktok-plans-big-push-into-gaming-conducting-tests-vietnam-sources-2022-05-19\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Reuters<\/a> said TikTok was testing HTML5 games in Vietnam, but TikTok"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/19\/tiktok-is-gearing-up-for-games-including-interactive-minigames-for-tiktok-live\/\">told<\/a> TechCrunch that was inaccurate — no games were currently testing in that market.<\/strong> However, the company had previously"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/09\/tiktok-ventures-into-mobile-gaming-initially-in-partnership-with-zynga\/\">confirmed<\/a> it was engaged in further gaming partnership discussions after its Zynga deal was announced.<\/li>\nTechCrunch"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/19\/tiktok-is-gearing-up-for-games-including-interactive-minigames-for-tiktok-live\/\">also reported and confirmed<\/a> a separate effort focused on bringing interactive minigames — like “Draw & Guess” — to the TikTok LIVE platform.<\/strong><\/li>\nNiantic\u2019s Pok\u00e9mon GO"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/19\/pokemon-go-amazon-prime-gaming-bonus\/\">partnered<\/a> with"https:\/\/gaming.amazon.com\/loot\/pokemongo\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Amazon Prime Gaming<\/a> and Prime Student to offer exclusive bonus item bundles every two weeks to Prime members.<\/strong> Users can log in to Prime and get a code, which they can redeem on Niantic\u2019s rewards page. The items will then appear in the game.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nSecurity & Privacy<\/h3>\n\nBrave’s iOS web browser was updated"https:\/\/brave.com\/1.38-release-ios\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">with a new Privacy Hub feature<\/a> <\/strong>that offers users more visibility on exactly what Brave blocked, and how Brave protects your personal information online. It does so by showing a rolling update of how many trackers Brave blocked on a specific site, or in a given time span. The hub also offers education about trackers and privacy threats.<\/li>\nApple"https:\/\/9to5mac.com\/2022\/05\/16\/apple-patches-27-security-flaws-ios-15-5\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">patched<\/a> almost 30 security flaws with iOS 15.5,<\/strong> as well as over 50 fixes for macOS 12.4.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nFunding and M&A<\/h1>\n\ud83d\udcb0 Pintarnya, a startup building a super app for Indonesia\u2019s blue-collar workers,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/pintarnya-is-building-a-super-app-for-indonesias-blue-collar-workers\/\">raised $6.3 million<\/a> in seed funding<\/strong> led by Sequoia Capital India and General Catalyst. The funding includes a $100,000 grant from Sequoia Spark, a program for women founders. The app offers verified job postings and financial services, like loans, for blue-collar workers.<\/p>\n\ud83d\udcb0 Instant delivery app Gopuff, valued at $15 billion,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/gopuff-the-instant-delivery-upstart-taps-ex-disney-head-bob-iger-as-its-newest-investor-and-advisor\/\">announced<\/a> a new advisor and investor: Bob Iger, the former CEO and chairman of The Walt Disney Company.<\/strong> The company wouldn’t say if the investment was coming as a separate investment, or as part of a $1 billion round (in debt and equity) that the company is in the process of closing.<\/p>\n\ud83d\udcb0 Instabug, a startup that helps mobile developers monitor, identify and fix bugs within apps,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/instabug-lands-46m-to-help-keep-your-apps-from-crashing\/\">raised $46 million<\/a> in Series B funding led by Insight Partners.<\/strong> The company said its ARR doubled in 2021 and the number of enterprise customers grew 10x, as it added new clients like DoorDash, Verizon, Qualtrics, Porsche and Gojek. Last year, its software sat within 2.7 billion mobile devices, processed 110 billion mobile sessions (up at least 20x from 2020) and helped customers resolve 4.2 billion issues, it said.<\/p>\n\ud83d\udcb0 Unit, a banking-as-a-service startup that allows developers to easily build new fintech apps,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/banking-as-a-service-startup-unit-closes-on-100m-at-a-1-2b-valuation\/\">raised $100 million<\/a> in Series C funding led by Insight Partners, at a $1.2 billion valuation.<\/strong> Unit said its transaction volume grew 7x over the past six months and has crossed an annualized transaction volume of $2.6 billion. It’s also issued over 430,000 cards to over 330,000 customers and saw a 10x increase in deposit volumes.<\/p>\n<\/p>\n"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/this-week-in-apps\/\">"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-1952542\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/02\/this-week-in-apps-banner2.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"93\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/02\/this-week-in-apps-banner2.png 2047w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/02\/this-week-in-apps-banner2.png?resize=150,21 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/02\/this-week-in-apps-banner2.png?resize=300,41 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/02\/this-week-in-apps-banner2.png?resize=768,105 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/02\/this-week-in-apps-banner2.png?resize=680,93 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/02\/this-week-in-apps-banner2.png?resize=1536,210 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/02\/this-week-in-apps-banner2.png?resize=50,7 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Welcome back to This Week in Apps, the weekly TechCrunch series that recaps the latest in mobile OS news, mobile applications and the overall app economy. Week In Apps","slug":"this-week-in-apps","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576701260"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576701260"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576701260"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576701260"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576701260"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2321911,"date":"2022-05-19T13:01:51","date_gmt":"2022-05-19T20:01:51","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2321911"},"modified":"2022-05-19T13:10:17","modified_gmt":"2022-05-19T20:10:17","slug":"snapchats-parental-control-features-near-launch-screenshots-show","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/19\/snapchats-parental-control-features-near-launch-screenshots-show\/","title":{"rendered":"Snapchat’s parental control features spotted in development"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Snapchat is preparing to introduce a new parental control feature dubbed “Family Center,” which will allow parents to see who their teen is friends with on the app as well as who they’ve been messaging with over the past seven days, and more.<\/p>\nSnap’s CEO Evan Spiegel first teased the planned offering"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/20\/snapchat-to-introduce-family-safety-tools-to-protect-minors-using-its-app\/\"> during an interview in October<\/a>, where he explained the feature would give parents better visibility into how teens use its service and, hopefully, make them feel more comfortable with the app.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"jHglvSyysK\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/20\/snapchat-to-introduce-family-safety-tools-to-protect-minors-using-its-app\/\">Snapchat to introduce family safety tools to protect minors using its app<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Snapchat to introduce family safety tools to protect minors using its app” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/20\/snapchat-to-introduce-family-safety-tools-to-protect-minors-using-its-app\/embed\/#?secret=xLZQS7Tw6c#?secret=jHglvSyysK\" data-secret=\"jHglvSyysK\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\nSnap is one of the last Big Tech social platforms to address the need for parental monitoring tools, though its app sees heavy use among younger users. At Snap’s"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/03\/snap-unveils-a-cameo-partnership-new-ad-format-and-more-original-programming\/\">NewFronts presentation<\/a> to advertisers earlier this month, the company noted the Snapchat app now reaches more than 75% of 13-34-year-olds in over 20 countries, and 80% of the U.S. Gen Z population had watched at least one of its Snap Original shows.<\/p>\nAccording to new screenshots of Snapchat’s forthcoming Family Center shared with TechCrunch by the product intelligence firm"https:\/\/watchful.ai\/\">Watchful<\/a>, the new Family Center feature allows parents to see who their teen is friends with on the app. This is useful for parents because, unlike many social networks, Snapchat’s friend lists aren’t public. Parents will also have visibility into who their teen has chatted with over the past seven days — but not the contents of those conversations. The screenshots additionally explain that parents will be able to assist their teen in reporting abuse and harassment, if needed.<\/p>\n"attachment_2322048\" style=\"width: 339px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2322048\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical size-large wp-image-2322048\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snapchat-family-center.jpg?w=329\" alt=\"\" width=\"329\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snapchat-family-center.jpg 608w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snapchat-family-center.jpg?resize=73,150 73w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snapchat-family-center.jpg?resize=145,300 145w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snapchat-family-center.jpg?resize=329,680 329w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snapchat-family-center.jpg?resize=24,50 24w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 329px) 100vw, 329px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2322048\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Snapchat screenshot via Watchful<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nThe parental control feature works by allowing parents to invite their teen (or teens) to the new in-app Family Center in order to begin the monitoring. The recipient of that invitation has the option of either accepting or declining the invitation.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nThis is, arguably, an appropriate approach to parental controls involving teens, as it respects their privacy. Instead of allowing parents to surreptitiously spy on their teens, it ensures the parent and child will instead have a conversation about parental monitoring, where they agree to a set of rules appropriate for their own household.<\/p>\nThe images provided by Watchful represent early designs of Snapchat’s feature, which is still in development and not yet live or being tested. We should note that products at this stage often change before their launch to the general public. That means the final product could look quite different. (The U.K. spelling of the word “Center,” too, suggests that we’re not seeing a global version of the Family Center product here.)<\/p>\n"attachment_2322047\" style=\"width: 346px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2322047\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical size-large wp-image-2322047\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snap-family-center.jpg?w=336\" alt=\"\" width=\"336\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snap-family-center.jpg 618w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snap-family-center.jpg?resize=74,150 74w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snap-family-center.jpg?resize=148,300 148w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snap-family-center.jpg?resize=336,680 336w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snap-family-center.jpg?resize=25,50 25w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 336px) 100vw, 336px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2322047\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Snapchat screenshot via Watchful<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nOther large social platforms have already launched their parental control features and other age-appropriate experiences for their younger users. Snap is running a little behind.<\/p>\nTikTok, for example, has"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/11\/17\/tiktok-expands-parental-controls-to-include-search-commenting-and-account-privacy\/\">continued to develop<\/a> its parental controls offerings following the"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/16\/tiktok-to-launch-parental-controls-globally-disable-direct-messaging-for-users-under-16\/\">debut of its in-app Family Pairing tool<\/a> back in 2020. The tool allows parents to pair their TikTok account with a child’s in order to control the account’s privacy, whether it’s suggested to other TikTok users, whether the child can use search, and who, if anyone, can view, comment or interact with the child’s content, among other things. There’s also a toggle to put the account into an even safer mode for under-13 users.<\/p>\nYouTube also"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/24\/youtube-to-launch-parental-control-features-for-families-with-tweens-and-teens\/\">launched parental control features<\/a> into testing last year that allow parents to select between different levels of YouTube access for teen or tween users. And Instagram arrived even later with its"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/16\/instagram-rolls-out-new-safety-tools-for-parents\/\">new safety tools for parents<\/a>, also called Family Center, which didn’t roll out until March 2022. Its tools let parents monitor time spent on the app, who has followed the child’s account and more.<\/p>\nAlthough all platforms compete broadly in the social media space, they all operate a bit differently, which informs what type of parental control features are actually needed. In Snapchat’s case, minors on the app have to mutually accept each other as friends before they can begin messaging. Minors’ accounts also aren’t shown in search results or as friend suggestions to another user — unless they have friends in common. And minors are not able to have public profiles. That means Snap wouldn’t need to roll out parental control features to control these types of experiences.<\/p>\nSnap declined to comment on the Family Center screenshots, but the company had previously said the offering would arrive in the coming months.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Snapchat is preparing to introduce a new parental control feature dubbed “Family Center,” which will allow parents to see who their teen is friends with on the app as well as who they’ve been messaging with over the past seven days, and more. Snap’s CEO Evan Spiegel first teased the planned offering during an interview is gearing up for games, including interactive minigames for TikTok LIVE"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">TikTok is already one of the"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/26\/tiktok-was-the-top-app-by-worldwide-downloads-in-q1-2022\/\">world’s fastest-growing<\/a> social media platforms, where it’s even"https:\/\/www.bbc.com\/news\/technology-58464745\">overtaken YouTube<\/a> on watch time in select markets and sports"https:\/\/newsroom.tiktok.com\/en-us\/1-billion-people-on-tiktok\">over 1 billion monthly active users<\/a>. Now, the company is looking to expand the range of activities its users can do when they tire of flipping through short videos. A report from"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/technology\/exclusive-tiktok-plans-big-push-into-gaming-conducting-tests-vietnam-sources-2022-05-19\/\">Reuters<\/a> today indicates the company is further investing in HTML5 games and has already begun tests. But we understand there may be more to TikTok’s gaming strategy than web-based gaming. It appears TikTok is also working on a LIVE mobile gaming feature that would allow creators to better engage fans while livestreaming.<\/p>\nReuters said TikTok planned to draw on parent company ByteDance’s suite of games, beginning with minigames that have simple mechanisms and a shorter playing time. It claimed tests had begun in Vietnam. But TikTok told TechCrunch that was inaccurate, saying that Vietnam gaming testing is not something it’s currently doing.<\/p>\nThe social video app’s move into HTML5 gaming was already known, as TikTok had previously announced its plans alongside its Zynga partnership last year. The two companies had teamed up to launch the HTML5 game Disco Loco 3D exclusively on TikTok. And at the time, TikTok confirmed it was"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/09\/tiktok-ventures-into-mobile-gaming-initially-in-partnership-with-zynga\/\">already in discussions<\/a> with other game makers for similar deals, telegraphing a larger gaming expansion was still to come. TikTok says it doesn’t have any new partners to name on this front as of now.<\/p>\n"attachment_2231447\" style=\"width: 1210px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2231447\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2231447 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/disco_loco_1200x675.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1200\" height=\"675\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/disco_loco_1200x675.jpg 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/disco_loco_1200x675.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/disco_loco_1200x675.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/disco_loco_1200x675.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/disco_loco_1200x675.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/disco_loco_1200x675.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2231447\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Zynga<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nAhead of the Zynga deal, TikTok had also already launched its own game, Garden of Good, built in partnership with nonprofit Feeding America and focused on charitable fundraising. This one felt more like an experiment to see if TikTok users would play an in-app game.<\/p>\nWhile still a smaller effort today, gaming could grow to become a significant monetization tool for TikTok, if the games end up being ad-supported or later add paid components, like in-app purchases.<\/p>\nIn addition to its previously announced efforts to delve into HTML5 games, TechCrunch has also learned TikTok is looking to explore LIVE games in a separate effort.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nAccording to an investigation by"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/06\/03\/watchful-is-a-mobile-product-intelligence-startup-that-surfaces-unreleased-features\/\">mobile product intelligence firm<\/a>"https:\/\/www.watchful.ai\/\">Watchful<\/a>, based in Tel Aviv, TikTok is working to add minigames to LIVE videos in its app to enhance the livestreaming experience between creators and their fans.<\/p>\nOne LIVE game Watchful uncovered is called Draw & Guess, which is designed specifically to encourage interaction between creators and viewers. In this Pictionary-like game, players are given words that they then draw on the screen, and viewers try to guess what they’re drawing. The correct guesses are shown on the screen.<\/p>\nWatchful also noted the mobile gaming feature may allow screen-sharing, so creators could share their screen with viewers in real time, including their camera, audio, notifications and other alerts. Their games could be shown in either landscape mode or portrait mode, the firm said.<\/p>\nWhile today, a handful of reverse engineers publicly share details of unannounced, still-in-development features they find in popular consumer apps, Watchful has productized this type of investigation and enhanced it with technology. The company uses a combination of computer vision and flow analysis to identify and emulate app changes. Its differential analysis engine compares application versions using real user data and proprietary computer vision algorithms, it says. The studies are also backed by the firm’s mobile device labs deployed around the world.<\/p>\nReached for comment, TikTok did not have anything more to share about the LIVE gaming efforts but told us it was a totally unrelated development from the HTML5 games Reuters had described.<\/p>\nGames aren’t the only way TikTok is looking to enhance the TikTok LIVE Platform.<\/p>\nWatchful also flagged another in-development feature that feels like a cross between a game and a virtual gifting experience. It allows users to add a “Treasure Box” to LIVE videos which doles out coins after a timer is up to a random set of users.<\/p>\n"attachment_2321755\" style=\"width: 307px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2321755\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical wp-image-2321755\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/eb581cd3-d69e-11ec-b9f1-097eea4a6a77.png?w=421\" alt=\"\" width=\"297\" height=\"480\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/eb581cd3-d69e-11ec-b9f1-097eea4a6a77.png 718w, class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> TikTok app image via Watchful<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nIt found TikTok was working on the in-app shopping experience, TikTok Shop, which is offered today in Indonesia, Malaysia, Thailand, Vietnam, mainland China, Hong Kong and the U.K. Here, TikTok appears to be looking at adding a shopping bag icon to LIVE shopping videos which, when clicked, opens up a window where viewers can browse through available products with the option to click to add them to a cart for immediate purchase.<\/p>\n"attachment_2321756\" style=\"width: 295px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2321756\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical wp-image-2321756\" ramps up revenue with global launch of Cloud API and soon, a paid tier for its Business App"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">WhatsApp is continuing its push into the business market with today’s news it’s launching the WhatsApp Cloud API to all businesses worldwide.
"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/01\/whatsapp-brings-its-business-api-to-the-cloud-to-speed-adoption\/\">Introduced into beta testing<\/a> last November, the new developer tool is a cloud-based version of the WhatsApp Business API — WhatsApp’s"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/08\/01\/whatsapp-business-api\/\">first revenue-generating enterprise product<\/a> — but hosted on parent company Meta’s infrastructure.<\/p>\nThe company had been building out its Business API platform over the past several years as one of the key ways the otherwise free messaging app would make money. Businesses pay WhatsApp on a per-message basis, with rates that vary based on the region and number of messages sent. As of late last year, tens of thousands of businesses were set up on the non-cloud-based version of the Business API including brands like Vodafone, Coppel, Sears Mexico, BMW, KLM Royal Dutch Airlines, Iberia Airlines, Itau Brazil, iFood, Bank Mandiri and others. This on-premise version of the API is free to use.<\/p>\nThe cloud-based version, however, aims to attract a market of smaller businesses and reduces the integration time from weeks to only minutes, the company had said. It is also free.<\/p>\nBusinesses integrate the API with their back-end systems, where WhatsApp communication is usually just one part of their messaging and communication strategy. They may also want to direct their communications to SMS, other messaging apps, emails and more. Typically, businesses would work with a solutions provider like Zendeks or Twilio to help facilitate these integrations. Providers during the cloud API beta tests had included Zendesk in the U.S., Take in Brazil and MessageBird in the E.U.<\/p>\nDuring Meta’s messaging-focused"https:\/\/metaconversations.me\/\">“Conversations” live event<\/a> today, Meta CEO Mark Zuckerberg announced the global, public availability of the cloud-based platform, now called the WhatsApp Cloud API.<\/p>\n“The best business experiences meet people where they are. Already more than 1 billion users connect with a business account across our messaging services every week. They’re reaching out for help, to find products and services, and to buy anything from big-ticket items to everyday goods. And today, I am excited to announce that we’re opening WhatsApp to any business of any size around the world with WhatsApp Cloud API,” he said.<\/p>\nHe said the company believes the new API will help businesses, both big and small, be able to connect with more people.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nIn addition to helping businesses and developers get set up faster than with the on-premise version, Meta says the Cloud API will help partners to eliminate costly server expenses and help them provide customers with quick access to new features as they arrive.<\/p>\nSome businesses may choose to forgo the API and use the dedicated WhatsApp Business app instead. Launched in 2018, the WhatsApp Business App is aimed at smaller businesses that want to establish an official presence on WhatsApp\u2019s service and connect with customers. It provides a set of features that wouldn’t be available to users of the free WhatsApp messaging app, like support automated quick replies, greeting messages, FAQs, away messaging, statistics and more.<\/p>\nToday, Meta is also introducing new power features for its WhatsApp Business app that will be offered for a fee — like the ability to manage chats across up to 10 devices. The company will also provide new customizable WhatsApp click-to-chat links that help businesses attract customers across their online presence, including of course, Meta’s other applications like Facebook and Instagram.<\/p>\nThese will be a part of a forthcoming Premium service for WhatsApp Business app users. Further details, including pricing, will be announced at a later date.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"WhatsApp is continuing its push into the business market with today’s news it’s launching the WhatsApp Cloud API to all businesses worldwide. Introduced into beta testing last November, the new developer tool is a cloud-based version of the WhatsApp Business API — WhatsApp’s first revenue-generating enterprise product — but hosted on parent company Meta’s infrastructure. Zuckerberg","slug":"mark-zuckerberg","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/341024"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=341024"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=341024"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=341024"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=341024"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":171,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/meta\/","name":"meta","slug":"meta","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/171"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=171"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=171"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=171"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=171"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2320932,"date":"2022-05-18T11:57:50","date_gmt":"2022-05-18T18:57:50","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2320932"},"modified":"2022-05-18T12:49:43","modified_gmt":"2022-05-18T19:49:43","slug":"youtube-teases-expansion-of-livestream-shopping-with-new-features-arriving-later-this-year","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/youtube-teases-expansion-of-livestream-shopping-with-new-features-arriving-later-this-year\/","title":{"rendered":"YouTube teases livestream shopping expansion with co-streams, live redirects"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">In recent years, YouTube has been working to transform its platform into more of a shopping destination with product launches like"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/06\/18\/youtube-announces-a-new-shoppable-ad-format\/\">shoppable ads<\/a> or more recently, the ability to"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/21\/youtube-to-pilot-test-shopping-from-livestreams-with-select-creators\/\">shop directly from livestreams<\/a> hosted by creators. Now, it’s furthering that investment with new features for live shopping experiences. At yesterday’s YouTube Brandcast event, where the company pitched itself to advertisers as a"https:\/\/www.tubefilter.com\/2022\/05\/17\/youtube-brandcast-upfronts-tv-mr-beast\/\">better place for their TV ad dollars<\/a>, YouTube teased upcoming features that it claimed would make it easier for viewers to discover and buy from brands.<\/p>\nThe company touted its forthcoming tools as offering advertisers a better way to engage viewers and make connections with their audience.<\/p>\nOne new feature, explained YouTube, will allow two creators to go live at the same time to co-host a single live shopping stream. This could effectively double the draw for the event, as each creator would bring their own fanbase to the stream.<\/p>\nThis feature arrives shortly after YouTube"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/watch?v=aIBCfaI-LwQ\">in March announced<\/a> a pilot program called “Go Live Together,” a new mobile collaborative streaming feature that would enable creators to invite guests to their livestream with a link before going live together. This trial suggested YouTube had its eye on developing tools to better power joint livestreams — just as it’s now planning to introduce with its upcoming two-person live shopping streams. The addition could also make YouTube more competitive with Instagram, which launched the ability for"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/01\/instagram-launches-live-rooms-for-live-broadcasts-with-up-to-four-creators\/\">creators to go live with up to three people<\/a> last year.<\/p>\nIn addition to leveraging creators to build an audience for a live shopping event, YouTube’s shopping livestreams platform also offers other tools specifically designed to drive sales. The brand-integrated shopping experience actually allows viewers to"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/21\/youtube-to-pilot-test-shopping-from-livestreams-with-select-creators\/\">shop the products shown in the video<\/a> by tapping on a built-in “view products” button that then brings up a list of items featured by the creators.<\/p>\nThe company says its new two-person live shopping feature will roll out sometime later this year.<\/p>\nAnother upcoming option announced at Brandcast is something YouTube calls “live redirects.”<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nIn this case, creators will be able to start a shopping livestream on their channel, then redirect their audience over to a brand’s channel for fans to keep watching. This allows brands to tap into the power of the creator’s platform and reach their fanbase, but then gives the brands themselves access to that audience — and the key metrics and analytics associated with their live event — directly on their own YouTube channel. This will also roll out sometime this year, says YouTube, but didn’t provide a timeframe.<\/p>\nYouTube’s announcements follow the"https:\/\/www.marketingdive.com\/news\/livestream-shopping-poised-grow-amid-demand-immersive-experiences\/616501\/\">broader growth<\/a> of the live e-commerce market in the U.S. — a trend inspired by the livestream shopping activity surging in China, where streamers can pull"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2021\/11\/16\/chinese-livestreamers-can-rake-in-billions-of-dollars-in-hours-how-long-will-it-last.html\">in billions of dollars in a matter of hours<\/a>. Today, a number of startups have also entered this space, including"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/08\/live-video-shopping-startup-talkshoplive-brings-in-another-6m\/\">TalkShopLive<\/a>,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/08\/popshop-live-raises-around-20m-at-a-100m-valuation-for-its-livestream-shopping-platform-for-hipsters\/\"> PopShop Live<\/a>,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/23\/livestream-video-shopping-app-ntwrk-raises-50m-from-goldman-sachs-kering\/\">NTWRK<\/a>,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/02\/fast-growing-livestream-shopping-platform-whatnot-acquires-pastel-labs-hires-vp-of-engineering\/\">Whatnot<\/a>,"https:\/\/www.retaildive.com\/news\/livestream-shopping-app-shopshops-raises-15m-for-us-expansion\/601689\/\">ShopShops<\/a>,"https:\/\/www.glossy.co\/beauty\/ulta-beauty-partners-with-livestream-shopping-app-supergreat\/\">Supergreat<\/a>\u00a0and others.
"https:\/\/www.modernretail.co\/retailers\/we-dont-want-to-be-seen-as-a-payments-company-only-klarna-unveils-virtual-shopping-offering\/\">Klarna even added<\/a> virtual shopping capabilities to connect its buy-now, pay-later customers with live product demos from retail partners.<\/p>\nRetailers, too, are getting in on the action.
"https:\/\/www.retaildive.com\/news\/nordstrom-debuts-interactive-livestreams\/596869\/\">Nordstrom launched<\/a> a live events platform, while"https:\/\/www.chainstoreage.com\/forever-21-pilots-livestream-shopping-app\">Forever 21<\/a> and"https:\/\/www.retaildive.com\/news\/macys-updates-app-launches-live-shopping\/607924\/\">Macy’s<\/a> are among those that added live shopping to their apps.<\/p>\nMeanwhile, big tech platforms are wooing brands by touting their wider reach.<\/p>\nOver the past year or so, we’ve seen"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/09\/walmart-to-host-a-new-live-stream-shopping-event-on-tiktok-following-successful-pilot\/\">Walmart pilot testing TikTok’s first livestreamed shopping<\/a> experience; Facebook’s live shopping boosting sales for brands like"https:\/\/www.retaildive.com\/news\/nordstrom-debuts-interactive-livestreams\/596869\/\">Petco<\/a>, Benefit, Samsung,"https:\/\/www.retaildive.com\/news\/facebook-debuts-shoppable-livestreams-with-anne-klein\/588899\/\">Anne Klein<\/a> and"https:\/\/www.facebook.com\/business\/success\/categories\/live-shopping\">others;<\/a> and Instagram hosting live shopping events to"https:\/\/www.socialmediatoday.com\/news\/instagram-launches-live-stream-shopping-events-for-the-holidays-free-shipp\/609338\/\">cater to holiday crowds.<\/a> Twitter even began to"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/22\/walmart-will-be-the-first-retailer-to-test-twitters-new-livestream-shopping-platform\/\">test livestream shopping<\/a>, also with Walmart’s help on its pilot run — but it’s unclear where such initiatives will land if the Elon Musk buyout comes to pass.<\/p>\nWhile YouTube is certainly one of the largest creator platforms for video, there is some indication that it needs to catch up to its big tech rivals in livestream shopping, however.
"https:\/\/www.emarketer.com\/content\/social-apps-livestream-shoppers\">An eMarketer study from Jan. 2022<\/a> found that only 14.4% of survey respondents said YouTube’s platform drove them to purchase during a livestream event compared with 15.8% for TikTok, 45.8% for Instagram and 57.8% for Facebook.<\/p>\n"attachment_2321091\" style=\"width: 480px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2321091\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2321091 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/273880.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"470\" height=\"371\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/273880.png 470w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/273880.png?resize=150,118 150w, 470px) 100vw, 470px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2321091\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> eMarketer\/Insider Intelligence<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nYouTube’s new livestream features — and particularly the one that pushes a creator’s fanbase to a brand’s channel — could make its solution more compelling.<\/p>\n“People come to YouTube every day to make decisions about what to buy, and 87% of viewers say that when they’re shopping or browsing on YouTube, they feel like they can make a faster decision about what to purchase because of all the information that we have in videos,” said YouTube CEO Susan Wojcicki, speaking to the audience at the Brandcast live event last night. “We have so much shopping activity that is already happening on YouTube, so we are making it even easier for viewers to discover and to buy,” she said.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"In recent years, YouTube has been working to transform its platform into more of a shopping destination with product launches like shoppable ads or more recently, the ability to shop directly from livestreams hosted by creators. Now, it’s furthering that investment with new features for live shopping experiences. and-more\/","title":{"rendered":"YouTube’s player gains new features including Most Replayed, Video Chapters, Single Loop and more"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">YouTube today is launching a new feature designed to help users identify the most popular parts of a video they’re watching, along with other changes for its video player. The company says it’s adding a graph that people can use to easily locate and watch the most replayed parts of a video — something that could be particularly helpful for longer videos or those that haven’t broken down their various sections using either timestamps or video chapters.<\/p>\nThe feature was previously available as an experiment that YouTube Premium subscribers could access from"http:\/\/youtube.com\/new\">YouTube.com\/New<\/a>, but it will now become available to all YouTube users, both free and Premium, across desktop, iOS and Android platforms.<\/p>\nWhile creators will often segment their longer videos into chapters or link to select parts via timestamps, the new graph aims to make it possible for users to scrub through any YouTube video to quickly find the most interesting parts. These segments may or not always correlate to where chapters or timestamps would be located, either — particularly in the case of certain video segments going viral, for example.<\/p>\nIn addition, the feature could help point users more to the useful parts of tutorial videos, or to the segment that has the most action — like the most watched bit of footage from a gamer’s video.<\/p>\nYouTube viewers will be able to now see this subtle gray graph as they scrub through the video using the red playback progress bar. If the graph is high, then that part of the video has been replayed often, says YouTube. The video thumbnail that appears will also indicate when you’ve hit the segment that is the “Most replayed.”<\/p>\n"attachment_2320895\" style=\"width: 324px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2320895\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical size-large wp-image-2320895\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/youtube-graph.png?w=314\" alt=\"\" width=\"314\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/youtube-graph.png 738w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/youtube-graph.png?resize=69,150 69w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/youtube-graph.png?resize=138,300 138w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/youtube-graph.png?resize=314,680 314w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/youtube-graph.png?resize=708,1536 708w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/youtube-graph.png?resize=23,50 23w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 314px) 100vw, 314px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2320895\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> YouTube<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nAlongside this launch, YouTube is also rolling out support for video chapters — the segmenting tool first launched in May 2020 — to smart TVs and gaming consoles. Chapters allow users to jump forward to a particular section of a video or easily rewatch that section. Since launching, YouTube has made it possible for chapters to be automatically generated and notes they’ve now been added to some 20 million videos to date.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nAnother newly added feature called Single Loop will now allow users to put an individual video on endless repeat. To access this feature, you’ll select the option from the same menu where you can adjust the video quality, turn on captions and more.<\/p>\nAlso, in full-screen mode, a new panel will now appear to display information about the video — like the video description, video chapters and comments. Users will be able to access quick action buttons here to like, dislike, comment, share or add a video to a playlist directly from full-screen mode.<\/p>\n"attachment_2320894\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2320894\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2320894\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/heatseeker.gif?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"334\" \/>"caption-attachment-2320894\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> YouTube<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nFinally, YouTube teased it will “soon” begin another new experiment that will allow users to seek the exact moment in a video that they want to watch. This, too, will first be made available to Premium subscribers via the YouTube.com\/New website, it says.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"YouTube today is launching a new feature designed to help users identify the most popular parts of a video they’re watching, along with other changes for its video player. player","slug":"video-player","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/103662"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=103662"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=103662"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=103662"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=103662"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":6567,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/youtube\/","name":"YouTube","slug":"youtube","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/6567"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=6567"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=6567"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=6567"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=6567"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2320755,"date":"2022-05-18T09:00:15","date_gmt":"2022-05-18T16:00:15","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2320755"},"modified":"2022-05-18T12:43:49","modified_gmt":"2022-05-18T19:43:49","slug":"tiktok-launches-its-first-creator-crediting-tool-to-help-video-creators-cite-their-inspiration","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/tiktok-launches-its-first-creator-crediting-tool-to-help-video-creators-cite-their-inspiration\/","title":{"rendered":"TikTok launches its first creator crediting tool to help video creators cite their inspiration"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">After years of stolen memes and uncredited dance trends, TikTok today is introducing a new feature that it says will be the first iteration of its creator crediting tools that allow creators to directly tag and credit others using a new button during the publishing process. This button lets creators credit all sorts of inspiration for their content, including dances, jokes, viral sounds and more — and will help TikTok viewers discover the original creators behind the latest trend by tapping on the credit from the video’s caption.<\/p>\nLarger creators lifting ideas from smaller ones is an issue that’s not limited to TikTok. But as one of the largest social apps on the market, particularly among a younger Gen Z to millennial demographic, how it approaches the issue of creator recognition matters.<\/p>\nTo that end, TikTok says it’s now rolling out a new feature that will allow users to add a credit as part of the publishing process on the app.<\/p>\n"attachment_2320818\" style=\"width: 324px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2320818\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical size-large wp-image-2320818\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/popup-FINAL.jpg?w=314\" alt=\"\" width=\"314\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/popup-FINAL.jpg 1500w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/popup-FINAL.jpg?resize=69,150 69w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/popup-FINAL.jpg?resize=139,300 139w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/popup-FINAL.jpg?resize=768,1663 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/popup-FINAL.jpg?resize=314,680 314w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/popup-FINAL.jpg?resize=709,1536 709w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/popup-FINAL.jpg?resize=946,2048 946w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/popup-FINAL.jpg?resize=23,50 23w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 314px) 100vw, 314px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2320818\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> TikTok<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nTo access the feature, users will tap on a new “video” icon on the posting page after creating or editing their own video. Once on the video page, users will be able to select a video they have liked, favorited, posted or that had used the same sound.<\/p>\nAfter this video is selected, the video tag will be added as a mention in the caption.<\/p>\nThose whose videos were tagged by another creator will then be alerted to this via an alert in their TikTok app Inbox.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n"attachment_2320819\" style=\"width: 324px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2320819\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical size-large wp-image-2320819\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/inbox-final.jpg?w=314\" alt=\"\" width=\"314\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/inbox-final.jpg 1500w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/inbox-final.jpg?resize=69,150 69w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/inbox-final.jpg?resize=139,300 139w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/inbox-final.jpg?resize=768,1663 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/inbox-final.jpg?resize=314,680 314w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/inbox-final.jpg?resize=709,1536 709w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/inbox-final.jpg?resize=946,2048 946w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/inbox-final.jpg?resize=23,50 23w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 314px) 100vw, 314px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2320819\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> TikTok<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nThe feature’s launch follows years of controversy over creator credits and attribution on TikTok.<\/p>\nIn particular, TikTok had struggled with some of its top stars sourcing new choreography to perform in their dance videos from creators on other, smaller platforms — like the rival short-form video app Dubsmash, later acquired by Reddit. Many of these unknown creators had helped kick off TikTok’s biggest dance trends in"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2020\/02\/13\/style\/the-original-renegade.html\">years past,<\/a> like the Renegade, Backpack Kid or Shiggy. And many were creators of color, who saw their dances go viral after more famous TikTokers would perform their moves without tagging them as the inspiration. This issue came to a head when"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2020\/02\/13\/style\/the-original-renegade.html\">The New York Times in 2020<\/a> reported on the original creator of the Renegade, then a 14-year-old Atlanta teen, Jalaiah Harmon, who hadn’t received credit for her work after TikTok’s largest creator, Charli D’Amelio, performed her dance for her millions of fans, helping her to further grow her already outsized celebrity status.<\/p>\nThe following year, a similar controversy made headlines after TikTok star"https:\/\/www.insider.com\/jimmy-fallon-addison-rae-tiktok-dance-black-creators-2021-3\">Addison Rae went on “The Tonight Show”<\/a> where she taught host Jimmy Fallon a number of popular TikTok dances. Meanwhile, the dances’ original creators, many of whom are Black, remained uncredited in the segment. Later, a number of Black creators"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2021\/06\/25\/style\/black-tiktok-strike.html\">went on strike<\/a> as part of a viral campaign to call attention to the issue of creator credits by refusing to choreograph a dance to Megan Thee Stallion\u2019s latest single.<\/p>\nD’Amelio and some other creators have since begun to handwrite dance credits in their video descriptions, often using the shorthand “dc” for dance credit followed by a tag pointing to the username of the creator. A famous Hollywood choreographer, JaQuel Knight, who made history as the first to copyright his work, has also begun helping other dancers on TikTok get credit for their work too,"https:\/\/www.vice.com\/en\/article\/g5qqkw\/black-tik-tok-tired-of-stolen-dances\">Vice reported<\/a> in December.<\/p>\nBut"https:\/\/www.buzzfeednews.com\/article\/tanyachen\/black-creators-on-tiktok-demanding-proper-dance-credits\"> dances<\/a> aren’t the only things being stolen on TikTok. Creators have fielded accusations of stealing everything from"https:\/\/www.elle.com\/culture\/a36178170\/black-tiktok-creators-mya-nicole-chris-cotter-addison-rae-jimmy-fallon\/\">cheerleading routines<\/a> to"https:\/\/www.dailydot.com\/unclick\/tiktoker-neumane-joey-bailey-stealing-content-accusations\/\">comedy bits<\/a> to"https:\/\/www.nbcnews.com\/pop-culture\/pop-culture-news\/months-after-tiktok-apologized-black-creators-many-say-little-has-n1256726\">challenge ideas<\/a> to"https:\/\/www.yahoo.com\/now\/2020-05-21-jason-derulo-savage-love-siren-beat-tiktok-song-stolen-joshua-nanai-24368998.html\">music<\/a> or sounds and much more.<\/p>\nA TikTok spokesperson acknowledged the problem with credits on the platform, noting that the culture of credit was “critical” for the community and for TikTok’s future. “Equitable creator amplification is important for creators, especially the BIPOC creator community,” they added.<\/p>\n"attachment_2320815\" style=\"width: 8010px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2320815\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2320815 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"8000\" height=\"4500\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg 8000w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Credit-Journey.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 8000px) 100vw, 8000px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2320815\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> TikTok<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nIn an announcement, Director of the Creator Community at TikTok Kudzi Chikumbu introduced the feature and highlighted other efforts the company has made to help better highlight original creator work on its platform.<\/p>\nChikumbu pointed to"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/@tiktok\/video\/7066117627143490863\">TikTok’s Originators series<\/a>, launched last October, which showcases trend originators through the app’s"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/creator-discover-list\/originators\/\">Discover List feature<\/a>. TikTok also\u00a0recently debuted a"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/@tiktok\/video\/7066117627143490863\">TikTok Originators monthly social series<\/a> highlighting Originators on the platform. In addition, the"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/creators\/creator-portal\/en-us\/foundations-for-success\/crediting-creators\/\">TikTok Creator Portal<\/a> includes a “Crediting Creators” section that highlights the importance of attributing trend originators for their work. Here, the company lays out best practices for crediting originators and explains how to find the originators if you aren’t sure who had started a trend.<\/p>\nThe use of the new crediting tag could help make it easier for creators to cite their inspiration. However, it still relies on user adoption to work. If a creator wants to lift ideas without credit, they could simply not use the feature.<\/p>\n“It’s important to see a culture of credit take shape across the digital landscape and to support underrepresented creators in being properly credited and celebrated for their work,” said Chikumbu. “We’re eager to see how these new creator crediting tools inspire more creativity and encourage trend attribution across the global TikTok community.”<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"After years of stolen memes and uncredited dance trends, TikTok today is introducing a new feature that it says will be the first iteration of its creator crediting tools that allow creators to directly tag and credit others using a new button during the publishing process.
