Media, the new media company co-backed by former Disney execs, acquires Gen Z-focused ATTN: for $100M"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Candle Media, the new media company headed by former Disney execs, Kevin Mayer and Tom Staggs, has made another acquisition — this time with an eye on social storytelling and reaching a Gen Z to millennial audience. The company announced today it will become the new owner of"https:\/\/www.attn.com\/\">ATTN:<\/a>, a media company that uses entertainment to discuss topical issues that help explain the world to a younger audience — particularly those who consume content on social media.<\/p>\nOf note, ATTN: also"https:\/\/www.attn.com\/updates\/24773\/attn-launches-tiktok-studio\/\">launched its own TikTok studio<\/a> last year to provide production services for brands that wanted to reach the TikTok user base. Clients on that effort have included big name brands like Google, Madewell, MTV and even TikTok itself, which partnered with ATTN: to manage its own “TikTok for Good” channel. That deal was recently renewed for a second year.<\/p>\nCandle explained its interest in ATTN: had to do with the company’s ability to effectively engage a social audience.<\/p>\n“ATTN: has a deep, digital-native understanding for how to cut through the noise and reach today\u2019s audiences through engaging content on social media. We are excited for them to join Candle and provide the benefits of their talented team\u2019s expertise across our brands and franchises,” read a statement by Candle co-CEOs, Mayer and Staggs.<\/p>\nLaunched in 2014, ATTN: has created original series for Facebook, Instagram, TikTok, YouTube and Twitch, in addition to networks ABC, NBC, CBS, MTV, Freeform and Discovery as well as for streaming services like Hulu and Apple TV. Its brand studio and agency have relationships with companies like Amazon, Ford, Google, Intel, Mattel, P&G, Target and T-Mobile.<\/p>\nThe acquisition offers ATTN: scale, capital and expertise to accelerate its growth, Candle Media said in a press release. ATTN: co-founders Matthew Segal and Jarrett Moreno, along with the existing senior management team, will continue to oversee day-to-day operations, original content, production and studio work, the announcement said.<\/p>\n"https:\/\/variety.com\/2022\/digital\/news\/attn-acquired-candle-media-100-million-1235269185\/\">Variety reports the deal<\/a> for ATTN: is around $100 million in both cash and stock but could be worth up to $150 million with additional earn-out provisions. Candle confirmed this figure to TechCrunch as well.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nBlackstone-backed, L.A.-based Candle Media was founded with an eye on aggregating brands to build an independent media operation — a rarity at a time when most media companies are now running their own streaming services.<\/p>\nIn an interview with"https:\/\/deadline.com\/2022\/04\/kevin-mayer-mip-tv-strategy-1234993921\/\">Deadline<\/a>, Mayer explained that Candle’s lack of a streamer was an important part of its strategy, as it believes demand for content itself is going to grow “extremely robustly” in the months ahead.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"GicPCKDZGO\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/02\/reese-witherspoons-hello-sunshine-sold-to-new-media-firm-from-former-disney-execs\/\">Reese Witherspoon’s Hello Sunshine sold to new media firm from former Disney execs<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Reese Witherspoon’s Hello Sunshine sold to new media firm from former Disney execs” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/02\/reese-witherspoons-hello-sunshine-sold-to-new-media-firm-from-former-disney-execs\/embed\/#?secret=j2rs5QKimv#?secret=GicPCKDZGO\" data-secret=\"GicPCKDZGO\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\nAfter coming onto the scene last year, the company has been making several high-profile acquisitions, including that of kids content company and “CoComelon” owner"https:\/\/variety.com\/2021\/biz\/news\/moonbug-acquisition-disney-tom-staggs-kevin-mayer-1235124553\/\">Moonbug for $3 billion<\/a>; “Fauda” maker Faraway Road Productions for"https:\/\/variety.com\/2022\/tv\/global\/candle-media-fauda-faraway-road-productions-1235152160\/\">somewhere south of $50 million<\/a>; and Reese Witherspoon’s"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/02\/reese-witherspoons-hello-sunshine-sold-to-new-media-firm-from-former-disney-execs\/\">Hello Sunshine for around $900 million<\/a>.<\/p>\nThis year, it also"https:\/\/www.livemint.com\/industry\/media\/candle-media-buys-stake-in-media-company-co-founded-by-will-smith-and-jada-pinkett-smith-11641386873627.html\">took a more than 10% stake<\/a> in Will Smith and Jada Pinkett Smith\u2019s media company, Westbrook, and was said to be"https:\/\/www.businessinsider.com\/blackstone-candle-media-kevin-mayer-tom-staggs-acquire-nft-notables-2022-5\">in talks to acquire NFT company Notables<\/a>.<\/p>\nCandle"https:\/\/tbivision.com\/2022\/01\/17\/candle-media-hires-disney-uta-execs-to-oversee-acquisitions-integration\/\">has also been hiring<\/a>, having recently added former\u00a0UTA and Disney execs as its chief development officer and CFO.<\/p>\nThe company says it expects the deal for ATTN: to close in about 30 days.<\/p>\nUpdated, 5\/17\/22, 5:06 PM ET with confirmation of deal price.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Candle Media, the new media company headed by former Disney execs, Kevin Mayer and Tom Staggs, has made another acquisition — this time with an eye on social storytelling and reaching a Gen Z to millennial audience. content","slug":"original-content","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/116227"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=116227"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=116227"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=116227"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=116227"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2320225,"date":"2022-05-17T12:19:49","date_gmt":"2022-05-17T19:19:49","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2320225"},"modified":"2022-05-18T16:29:50","modified_gmt":"2022-05-18T23:29:50","slug":"netflix-lays-off-150-staffers-citing-slowing-revenue-growth","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/netflix-lays-off-150-staffers-citing-slowing-revenue-growth\/","title":{"rendered":"Netflix lays off 150 staffers, citing slowing revenue growth"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Netflix confirmed it’s laid off approximately 150 primarily U.S.-based staffers as it works to rein in costs as its top-line growth has slowed down.<\/p>\nA Netflix representative wrote in an emailed statement, \u201cAs we explained on earnings, our slowing revenue growth means we are also having to slow our cost growth as a company. So sadly, we are letting around 150 employees go today, mostly U.S.-based. These changes are primarily driven by business needs rather than individual performance, which makes them especially tough as none of us want to say goodbye to such great colleagues. We’re working hard to support them through this very difficult transition.\u201d<\/p>\n"https:\/\/deadline.com\/2022\/05\/netflix-layoffs-us-employees-1235026085\/\">Deadline<\/a> had reported that some of those let go were in creative, including in original content. Reportedly, directors from the original series area, such as Sebastian Gibbs and Negin Salmasi, were among those let go, its report said.<\/p>\nSeparately, TechCrunch learned that there have been some changes to animated projects, which could impact around 70 employees in the animation division. These were not included in the 150 figure.<\/p>\nWe asked Netflix about the allegations shared on Twitter that the layoffs had targeted social channels designed to bring marginalized viewers to the service. One such"https:\/\/twitter.com\/freeblackgirl\/status\/1526674760674861056\">tweet<\/a> had named channels like Strong Black Lead, Golden, Most, and Con Todo as being impacted by this headcount reduction.<\/p>\nNetflix clarified thatnone<\/em> of its social channels — including those mentioned on Twitter and others (eg. Geeked, Netflix Family, Netflix is a Joke, etc.) — would be shut down. The company said those channels would continue to be staffed and run by full-time Netflix employees as they had before.<\/p>\nWhat did happen, however, is that Netflix decided not to renew contracts with select agencies that it previously used to source contractors for its publishing and social arms. With those deals terminated, there was a reduction in the number of contractors working across all Netflix’s social channels. These contractors are not included in Netflix’s count of 150 roles terminated as that figure is specifically related to Netflix’s employee numbers. As such, the layoffs have not changed Netflix’s makeup from a DEI perspective, as its reporting here looks at full-time staff. The company says people of color continue to make up about 50% of its U.S. and Canadian full-time workforce and women make up around 48% of staff.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nThe company declined to say how many contractors were impacted by the agency contract terminations.<\/p>\nAfter publication, the Netflix Twitter account"https:\/\/twitter.com\/netflix\/status\/1527003485304197122?s=21&t=1plZKutQMT5x8r17O1MQcQ\">announced<\/a> that none of the social channels were closing and would continue with “voices celebrating — and from — those communities.”<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Your favorite Black, LGBTQ+, API, and Latinx stories will always have a home on"https:\/\/twitter.com\/strongblacklead?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@strongblacklead<\/a>"https:\/\/twitter.com\/Most?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@Most<\/a>"https:\/\/twitter.com\/netflixgolden?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@netflixgolden<\/a> &"https:\/\/twitter.com\/contodonetflix?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@contodonetflix<\/a>, with voices celebrating – and from – those communities.
"https:\/\/t.co\/mJcMfXbKgT\">pic.twitter.com\/mJcMfXbKgT<\/a><\/p>\n— Netflix (@netflix)"https:\/\/twitter.com\/netflix\/status\/1527003485304197122?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">May 18, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\nIn a statement, a Netflix spokesperson said “We are making changes to how we support our publishing efforts, including bringing some of this important work in-house. Our social channels continue to grow and innovate, and we are investing heavily in them.”<\/p>\nThe agency contract terminations had also impacted Netflix’s"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/28\/netflix-layoffs-tudum-editorial\/\">recent marketing layoffs<\/a> when 25 full-time employees people were let go. Netflix’s newer site Tudum had been impacted by the marketing cuts, as were other marketing roles. (This round of layoffs had also included a mix of full-time employees and contractors, but 25 was the number of full-time employees impacted.)<\/p>\nStaff reductions had been expected, as the company said in its quarterly"https:\/\/s22.q4cdn.com\/959853165\/files\/doc_financials\/2022\/q1\/FINAL-Q1-22-Shareholder-Letter.pdf\">letter to shareholders<\/a>, \u201cOur revenue growth has slowed considerably as our results and forecast below show.\u201d<\/p>\nNetflix reported revenue of $7.87 billion for the first quarter of 2022 and a significant loss of"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/19\/netflix-shares-down-more-than-20-after-losing-200000-subscribers-in-first-quarter\/\">200,000 subscribers<\/a>. Analysts had predicted $7.93 billion and 2.7 million subscribers. A belt-tightening was on the horizon as soon as those quarterly figures hit.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"JnVTXG3o3V\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/19\/netflix-shares-down-more-than-20-after-losing-200000-subscribers-in-first-quarter\/\">Netflix shares down more than 20% after losing 200,000 subscribers in first quarter<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Netflix shares down more than 20% after losing 200,000 subscribers in first quarter” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/19\/netflix-shares-down-more-than-20-after-losing-200000-subscribers-in-first-quarter\/embed\/#?secret=dW7LIPlD0V#?secret=JnVTXG3o3V\" data-secret=\"JnVTXG3o3V\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\nCost-cutting measures were also addressed by Netflix CFO Spencer Neumann during the latest earnings call.<\/p>\nHe said, \u201c \u2026 presumably, for the next 18, 24 months, call it the next two years, we\u2019re kind of operating to roughly that operating margin, which does mean that we\u2019re pulling back on some of our spend growth across both content and non-content spend, but still growing our spend and still investing aggressively into that long-term opportunity.”<\/p>\nNeumann added, \u201cWe\u2019re trying to be smart about it and prudent in terms of pulling back on some of that spending growth to reflect the realities of the revenue growth of the business.\u201d<\/p>\nNetflix has been scrambling as of late, cracking down on"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/19\/netflix-to-charge-global-members-sharing-their-accounts-an-additional-fee-following-tests\/\">password sharing<\/a> and announcing a"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/10\/netflix-could-introduce-its-ad-supported-plan-as-soon-as-this-year\/\">cheaper ad-supported tier<\/a> in hopes of gaining new subscribers and driving further growth.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ki3JHnEsz9\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/28\/netflix-layoffs-tudum-editorial\/\">Netflix layoffs hit Tudum, its editorial arm, just five months after launch<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Netflix layoffs hit Tudum, its editorial arm, just five months after launch” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/28\/netflix-layoffs-tudum-editorial\/embed\/#?secret=bLyN8ZIx7W#?secret=ki3JHnEsz9\" data-secret=\"ki3JHnEsz9\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<\/p>\nUpdated 5\/17\/22 at 6:05 p.m. Updated list of names impacted to remove Brooke Kessler, which had been cited by another outlet; 5\/18\/22, 9:10 AM ET with additional insight into the layoffs metrics; and again at 5\/18\/22, 7:29 PM ET with Netflix tweet, statement, and further clarification around animation dept.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Netflix confirmed it’s laid off approximately 150 primarily U.S.-based staffers as it works to rein in costs as its top-line growth has slowed down. the maker of an automatic Slack status updater, acquires team communication startup Lounge"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">"https:\/\/lounge.place\/\">Lounge<\/a>, a team communication startup that was looking to"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/22\/lounges-new-app-aims-to-reimagine-the-office-for-the-remote-work-era\/\">reimagine the future of work<\/a> with features designed for remote and distributed workforces, has now found an exit after Slack"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/30\/slacks-new-video-and-voice-tools-are-nod-to-changing-face-of-work\/\">entered its same market<\/a> last year with competitive voice and video tools. Launched by former Life360 employees"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/22\/lounges-new-app-aims-to-reimagine-the-office-for-the-remote-work-era\/\">last year,<\/a> Lounge confirmed it’s been acquired for an undisclosed sum by"https:\/\/getpulse.team\/\">Pulse<\/a> — another company building technology aimed at improving remote worker productivity, but specifically through features that automate updates to users’ Slack status via a combination of AI and custom rules.<\/p>\nPulse was founded by"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/in\/rajansingh\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https:\/\/www.google.com\/url?q=https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/in\/rajansingh\/&source=gmail&ust=1650981158979000&usg=AOvVaw2AnIuIzcg_ILb1ZwqcO-d6\">Raj Singh<\/a>, who has already had multiple"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2015\/05\/29\/salesforce-acquires-tempo\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https:\/\/www.google.com\/url?q=https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2015\/05\/29\/salesforce-acquires-tempo\/&source=gmail&ust=1650981158979000&usg=AOvVaw3nWVCkcboJz9eoxaR8J1Fu\">exits, including to companies like Salesforce<\/a>. In particular, Pulse was attracted to Lounge’s ideas around team-building activities for remote workers.<\/p>\nThat was only a subset of what Lounge had offered, however. Its service was a more expansive platform with features like message boards, audio chat, group audio and visual representations of typical corporate office spaces — like employee desks, conference rooms and even break rooms. On top of this, it had built features designed to help remote workers connect and get to know one another, like photo-sharing tools and support for company-wide events — like steps or meditation challenges, for example.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"hWyFeXtPW4\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/22\/lounges-new-app-aims-to-reimagine-the-office-for-the-remote-work-era\/\">Lounge’s new app aims to reimagine the office for the remote work era<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Lounge’s new app aims to reimagine the office for the remote work era” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/22\/lounges-new-app-aims-to-reimagine-the-office-for-the-remote-work-era\/embed\/#?secret=pyauYlG1mr#?secret=hWyFeXtPW4\" data-secret=\"hWyFeXtPW4\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\nAccording to Lounge CEO Alex Kwon, despite his startup’s unique features, it struggled against the lock-in and network effect of mainstream remote work platforms, like Slack and Microsoft Teams. But the final bullet was Slack’s introduction of Huddle, its own"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/30\/slacks-new-video-and-voice-tools-are-nod-to-changing-face-of-work\/\">lightweight audio networking feature<\/a> that effectively took aim at one of Lounge’s biggest selling points — drop-in voice chats.<\/p>\nInitially, Lounge decided to pivot to focus more on asynchronous team-building activities with deeper Slack integration.<\/p>\nKwon says Singh later reached out to him and explained how Pulse aimed to become a platform for displaying the status of each team member right inside Slack, where they’re already working — as opposed to having employees use a whole new platform like Lounge. Pulse was also looking to expand its solution to other workplace apps, like Microsoft Teams, Google Workspace and even Discord. Both parties agreed that establishing team-building activities as a social layer for this existing offering could make sense. It also served Lounge’s original vision to make remote teams feel closer.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n“Raj is an experienced entrepreneur in the B2B space with a previous exit to Salesforce, so the acquisition conversation became a natural next step for us,” notes Kwon.<\/p>\nPulse aims to use Lounge’s asynchronous team-building activities like its Steps challenge and Team photos feature as the social roadmap for Pulse’s ambient status updater right inside Slack, Kwon says. You could imagine, then, how companywide team-building challenges could be turned into Slack status updates the same way Pulse today updates your status based on the apps you use — like Zoom, Google Meet, Skype, Slack Huddles, etc. — and your calendar, working hours and more.<\/p>\nAs a result of the acquisition, Kwon is the only Lounge member joining Pulse, and only as a part-time product adviser — a signal the acquisition was more about the tech than talent.<\/p>\nDeal terms weren’t revealed but we understand it to be more stock than cash, implying a smaller exit.<\/p>\nLounge had raised $1.2 million in funding from investors including Unusual Ventures, Hustle Fund, Translink, Unpopular Ventures and other angels.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Lounge, a team communication startup that was looking to reimagine the future of work with features designed for remote and distributed workforces, has now found an exit after Slack entered its same market last year with competitive voice and video tools. Launched by former Life360 employees last year, Lounge confirmed it’s been acquired for an work","slug":"remote-work","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/970347"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=970347"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=970347"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=970347"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=970347"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":251552,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/slack\/","name":"slack","slug":"slack","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/251552"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=251552"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=251552"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=251552"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=251552"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":449557042,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/startups\/","name":"Startups","slug":"startups","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449557042"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557042"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2319827,"date":"2022-05-17T08:34:59","date_gmt":"2022-05-17T15:34:59","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2319827"},"modified":"2022-05-17T13:18:14","modified_gmt":"2022-05-17T20:18:14","slug":"psa-apples-new-rules-let-apps-raise-subscription-prices-automatically","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/psa-apples-new-rules-let-apps-raise-subscription-prices-automatically\/","title":{"rendered":"PSA: Apple’s new rules let apps raise subscription prices automatically"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Surely, this won’t be abused? Alongside the"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/16\/ios-15-5-apple-cash-update-send-request-money-wallet\/\">launch of the iOS 15.5 update<\/a>, Apple"https:\/\/developer.apple.com\/news\/?id=tpgp89cl\">introduced<\/a> a new set of rules to govern auto-renewing subscriptions on the App Store. Now, instead of asking users to agree to any subscription price increases, developers will be able to roll out a price increase without the user’s explicit consent. The feature feels somewhat anti-consumer, as it allows developers to simply inform customers they’ll be charged more, not require the customer to opt-in to the higher pricing.<\/p>\nTechCrunch first broke the news that Apple was"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/05\/apple-pilot-tests-feature-that-allows-developers-to-automatically-charge-users-for-subscription-price-increases\/\">pilot testing this program<\/a> last month, when it appeared Disney+ subscription customers had simply been told their price was increasing but weren’t asked for their consent. Apple then confirmed this was the result of a “new commerce feature” it planned to launch soon, which it said would be “great for both developers and users.”<\/p>\nIt’s certainly great for developers! For users, maybe not so much.<\/p>\nApple’s position on the matter is that it could save consumers the hassle of having their subscriptions automatically canceled just because they didn’t see the notification or email that asked them to opt in to the price increase.<\/p>\n“This has led to some services being unintentionally interrupted for users and they must take steps to resubscribe within the app, from Settings on iPhone and iPad, or in the App Store on Mac,” the company"https:\/\/developer.apple.com\/news\/?id=tpgp89cl\">explained<\/a> in its announcement on Monday.<\/p>\nHowever, the flip side of this argument is that those same customers who would have missed the consent notification will likely be the same ones who would now miss the notification informing them their subscription will be increasing in price.<\/p>\nThese may include customers who don’t keep a close eye on their inboxes and tend to miss Apple’s emails; those who keep their iOS notifications silenced or aggregated into summaries using Apple’s own notification management tools; as well as those who so infrequently use a particular subscription-based app that they would likely rather have their subscription lapse than be automatically opted in to paying more.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nThere’s also an argument here that this change could enable unscrupulous developers and scammers to better profit from their victims. Although Apple reviews apps for adherence to its App Store policies as part of its vetting process, it has"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/10\/15\/sneaky-subscriptions-are-plaguing-the-app-store\/\">for years<\/a>"https:\/\/www.theverge.com\/2021\/4\/21\/22385859\/apple-app-store-scams-fraud-review-enforcement-top-grossing-kosta-eleftheriou\">struggled<\/a> to rein in subscription scams. There are still a number of apps operating on the App Store that are"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/03\/apple-urged-to-root-out-rating-scams-as-developer-highlights-ugly-cost-of-enforcement-failure\/\">leveraging fake reviews<\/a> to give their app the appearance of being well received in order to scam users out of their money.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"mvOENrZi0f\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/22\/apple-downplays-complaints-about-app-store-scams-in-antitrust-hearing\/\">Apple downplays complaints about App Store scams in antitrust hearing<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Apple downplays complaints about App Store scams in antitrust hearing” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/22\/apple-downplays-complaints-about-app-store-scams-in-antitrust-hearing\/embed\/#?secret=NC3n4GR2BH#?secret=mvOENrZi0f\" data-secret=\"mvOENrZi0f\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\nIn"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/22\/apple-downplays-complaints-about-app-store-scams-in-antitrust-hearing\/\">an antitrust hearing last year,<\/a> Congress even questioned Apple why it was not able to locate the fraudulent apps and scams, given they were “trivially easy to identify.” Instead, the wider public was only learning of the scams through “open-source reporting and journalists,” noted Georgia\u2019s Senator Jon Ossoff at the time. Apple demurred, and insisted that it had invested millions in hardening its App Store’s security.<\/p>\nBut today, subscription scams continue to persist. And, unfortunately, this new policy change could increase the damage done by those bad actors.<\/p>\nApple, at least, built in a few protections to the new program so the feature can’t be egregiously abused. It says developers can’t increase prices more than once per year. The increase also can’t exceed 50% of the subscription price, and the difference in price can’t exceed $5 USD per period for non-annual subscriptions or $50 USD for annual subscriptions. It also must be permitted by local laws.<\/p>\nThe company also says users will be warned of the price increase in advance via email, push notification and a message within the app. And Apple will notify users of how to view, manage and cancel subscriptions if they don’t want to pay more. It’s unclear how Apple will police this program to ensure scammers aren’t increasing prices more frequently than permitted or at higher rates that would otherwise require consent. Hopefully, Apple will keep a strict eye on the apps adopting this option.<\/p>\nApple may have chosen to enact the policy to better cater to the larger app developers who are pushing for new regulations that would allow them to collect subscription payments without having to use Apple’s own in-app purchasing system, which requires a rev share with the tech giant. These companies want to control their own customer relationships and manage their own payments — control that could include doling out the occasional price increase without having to regain the consent of their entire subscription base each time.<\/p>\nWhile some developers may welcome Apple’s latest change to save themselves the trouble of having to gather consent for smaller price changes, others are likely worried about the potential for abuse — particularly because that abuse could have long-term negative impacts on consumers’ willingness to subscribe to apps in the first place.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Surely, this won’t be abused? Alongside the launch of the iOS 15.5 update, Apple introduced a new set of rules to govern auto-renewing subscriptions on the App Store. Now, instead of asking users to agree to any subscription price increases, developers will be able to roll out a price increase without the user’s explicit consent. /tags\/31381487"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=31381487"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=31381487"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=31381487"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=31381487"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576888305,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/ios-15\/","name":"iOS 15","slug":"ios-15","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576888305"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576888305"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576888305"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576888305"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576888305"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2319143,"date":"2022-05-17T06:53:34","date_gmt":"2022-05-17T13:53:34","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2319143"},"modified":"2022-05-17T13:17:36","modified_gmt":"2022-05-17T20:17:36","slug":"snapchats-stricter-policies-for-anonymous-apps-and-friend-finders-arent-yet-fully-enforced","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/snapchats-stricter-policies-for-anonymous-apps-and-friend-finders-arent-yet-fully-enforced\/","title":{"rendered":"Snapchat’s stricter policies for anonymous apps and friend finders aren’t yet fully enforced"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">A small handful of Snap Kit platform developers have not yet complied with the new guidelines around anonymous messaging and friend-finding apps"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/following-suicides-and-lawsuits-snapchat-restricts-apps-building-on-its-platform-with-new-policies\/\">announced in March<\/a>. The Snapchat maker revamped its developer platform policies on March 17, 2022, to ban anonymous apps and require developers to build friend-finding apps to limit access to users 18 or older. The policy changes were effective immediately and existing developers were given 30 days to come into compliance — a date that would have passed last month.<\/p>\nIt is now mid-May and some developers of the newly banned and restricted apps are not yet meeting Snap’s new requirements, we’ve found.<\/p>\nSnap says only a small number of developers asked for and were granted additional time to bring apps into compliance, as they worked in good faith to make the necessary changes. But it may be difficult for consumers to tell which apps are compliant, which are skirting the new rules and which are marketing Snap Kit integrations that they actually don’t have.<\/p>\nFor example, one of the apps offered an extension is Sendit, the anonymous Q&A app that"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/03\/anonymous-snapchat-app-sendit-surges-with-3-5m-installs-after-snap-bans-yolo-and-lmk\/\">surged to the top of the App Store<\/a> last year after Snap"https:\/\/www.latimes.com\/business\/technology\/story\/2021-05-11\/snapchat-suspends-yolo-lmk\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">suspended<\/a> other top anonymous Q&A apps, YOLO and LMK. Those latter two apps had been banned from Snap’s platform after the company was sued by a mother of a teen who died by suicide after being bullied via those tools. This year, Snap was named in a"https:\/\/www.washingtonpost.com\/nation\/2022\/01\/22\/selena-rodriguez-suicide-meta-snap-lawsuit\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">second lawsuit<\/a>, alongside Meta, related to an alleged lack of safeguards across social media platforms which a mother says contributed to her 11-year-old’s suicide.<\/p>\nSnap has since conducted a review of its platform policies with a focus on potential child safety issues related to third-party apps that integrate with Snapchat’s features and functionality.<\/p>\nThis culminated in the"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/following-suicides-and-lawsuits-snapchat-restricts-apps-building-on-its-platform-with-new-policies\/\">new policies<\/a> that were introduced in March which impact apps that build using the"https:\/\/kit.snapchat.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Snap Kit platform.<\/a> This suite of developer tools allows third-party apps to offer sign-in with Snapchat for user verification, or utilize Snapchat features like Snap’s Camera, Bitmoji, Stories and more.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"oWkFug5ML7\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/03\/anonymous-snapchat-app-sendit-surges-with-3-5m-installs-after-snap-bans-yolo-and-lmk\/\">Sendit gains 3.5M downloads after Snapchat suspends top anonymous apps YOLO and LMK<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Sendit gains 3.5M downloads after Snapchat suspends top anonymous apps YOLO and LMK” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/03\/anonymous-snapchat-app-sendit-surges-with-3-5m-installs-after-snap-bans-yolo-and-lmk\/embed\/#?secret=ei3ySNedDq#?secret=oWkFug5ML7\" data-secret=\"oWkFug5ML7\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\nAt the time Snap"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/17\/following-suicides-and-lawsuits-snapchat-restricts-apps-building-on-its-platform-with-new-policies\/\">announced<\/a> its new policies, it said the changes would impact a small subset of its over 1,500 developers in its wider community. Around 2% would be impacted by the ban on anonymous messaging apps, Snap said, and another 3% would be impacted by the new requirement to age-gate friend-finding apps.<\/p>\nSendit appeared to be non-compliant as it was not utilizing a required feature, as specified"https:\/\/docs.snap.com\/snap-kit\/creative-kit\/Tutorials\/ios\/#identity-web-view\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">by Snap’s own developer documentation<\/a>.<\/p>\nHere, Snap offered an example of how something called “Identity Web View” could be adopted by third-party developers who today use Snap Kit to build anonymous Q&A apps. The feature would allow anonymous Q&A apps to come into compliance with the new policies as it will require apps to present a new modal to users that they must click to send their Bitmoji avatar URL and abbreviated Display Name to the third-party application. Then, they can use the third-party app to post their question — but no longer anonymously. Essentially, it allows Q&A apps to continue to function in much the same way as before, but without the potential dangers of anonymous bullying — the user is identified.<\/p>\nSendit, however, doesn’t currently use this modal even though it’s the example shown in the developer documentation screenshot. But Snap says the developer asked for more time to make these changes, which was granted. Snap believes the app, currently No. 8 in the Lifestyle section on the App Store, will soon come into compliance.<\/p>\n"attachment_2319275\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2319275\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2319275\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snap-ux-for-compliance.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"506\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snap-ux-for-compliance.jpg 1676w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snap-ux-for-compliance.jpg?resize=150,112 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snap-ux-for-compliance.jpg?resize=300,223 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snap-ux-for-compliance.jpg?resize=768,572 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snap-ux-for-compliance.jpg?resize=680,506 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snap-ux-for-compliance.jpg?resize=1536,1144 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/snap-ux-for-compliance.jpg?resize=50,37 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2319275\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Snap, via"https:\/\/docs.snap.com\/snap-kit\/creative-kit\/Tutorials\/ios\/#adding-captions-stickers-or-url-attachments-to-photos-or-videos\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Snapchat Developer documentation<\/a><\/p><\/div><\/p>\nOther third-party apps also appear to be still operating as usual and, at first glance, seem to not be in compliance with Snap’s new policies.<\/p>\nApps skirting the rules — or operating outside them?<\/h3>\nBut this is where things get more tricky — some apps have been granted an extension, some are routing around Snap’s rules and others are marketing themselves as Snapchat-connected apps when they’re not actually using the SDK.<\/p>\nFor instance, the app"https:\/\/apps.apple.com\/us\/app\/lmk-anonymous-polls\/id1465092216\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">LMK<\/a> — to be clear, adifferent<\/em> LMK than the original LMK app that was"https:\/\/www.latimes.com\/business\/technology\/story\/2021-05-11\/snapchat-suspends-yolo-lmk\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">banned<\/a> last year — is still offering"https:\/\/apps.apple.com\/us\/app\/lmk-anonymous-polls\/id1465092216\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">its “anonymous polls” app<\/a> which integrates with Snapchat’s features. The app is rated 12+ on the App Store and is functioning as usual. But LMK was among those that requested and was granted an extension.<\/p>\nAnonymous messaging apps"https:\/\/apps.apple.com\/us\/app\/hmu-create-mess-fun\/id1591908473\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">HMU<\/a>, rated ages 9+ on the App Store, and"https:\/\/apps.apple.com\/us\/app\/intext-anonymous-q-a\/id1596909817\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Intext,<\/a> rated ages 4+, are also still operating. Both advertise themselves as Snapchat-connected apps. But Intext has been banned from Snap’s platform — you’ll get an error if you try to authenticate with Snapchat using the app’s “Login with Snapchat” button.<\/p>\nHMU appears to have skirted the ban, however, as its app was working until some time yesterday when it was banned.<\/p>\nMeanwhile, a number of friend-finding apps, like"https:\/\/apps.apple.com\/us\/app\/hoop-make-new-friends\/id1442571346\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Hoop<\/a>,"https:\/\/apps.apple.com\/us\/app\/wink-make-new-friends\/id1482681335\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Wink<\/a>,"https:\/\/apps.apple.com\/us\/app\/swipr-make-new-friends\/id1537012560\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Swipr<\/a>,"https:\/\/apps.apple.com\/us\/app\/purp-make-new-friends\/id1562883907\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Purp<\/a> and"https:\/\/apps.apple.com\/us\/app\/dope-friends-for-snapchat\/id1582439585\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dope<\/a> — all of which are now supposed to be only available to adult users — are still published on the App Store with an age rating of 12+, as of the time of writing. If Snap had vetted and approved them, then they would have the highest age rating on the App Store, which is 17+. (Apple should change this to 18+!)<\/p>\nConfusingly, these apps’ lower age ratings don’t necessarily mean all the apps are breaking Snap’s policies. As it turns out, some of these apps are simplypositioning<\/em> themselves as being Snapchat-connected in their marketing materials — like their App Store screenshots. But in reality, they’re working around their lack of access to Snap’s SDK in other ways.<\/p>\nFor instance, Hoop’s App Store page says it’s for making friends on Snapchat, and yet it’s downloadable to anyone aged 12 or up. If it was a Snap Kit platform app, then it would be in violation. But Hoop is not in violation because it’s no longer using the SDK. (But who could tell?!)<\/p>\n"attachment_2319429\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2319429\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2319429 size-large\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-16-at-4.16.38-PM.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"466\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-16-at-4.16.38-PM.jpg 759w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-16-at-4.16.38-PM.jpg?resize=150,103 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-16-at-4.16.38-PM.jpg?resize=300,206 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-16-at-4.16.38-PM.jpg?resize=680,466 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-16-at-4.16.38-PM.jpg?resize=50,34 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2319429\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Hoop<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nInstead, Hoop has users enter their Snapchat username during onboarding and provides an in-app Snapchat button to “request” someone share their username with you. It’s a workaround that allows the app to still function as a tool for finding friends on Snapchat, but allows the app to operate without relying on developer access to the SDK. But this sort of deviousness on developers’ parts could cause complications for Snap in the future, as it faces potential litigation and regulations related to platform safety.<\/p>\nRequests for comment to the third-party app makers themselves were not returned.<\/p>\nFor parents, this lack of consistency across the Snapchat app ecosystem also means they can’t rely on using Apple or Google’s built-parental controls to block the Snapchat friend-finding apps from being downloaded to their child or younger teen’s device. And, once in the hands of younger users, bypassing the age-gate is as simple as using a fake birthdate.<\/p>\nSnap tells us that since it announced the new policies, it has removed the vast majority of apps that were out of compliance with its policies.<\/p>\n“First and foremost, we put the privacy and safety of our community first and expect the products built by our developer community to adhere to that standard in addition to bringing fun and positive experiences to people,” said Alston Cheek, director of Platform Partnerships at Snap. “We believe that we can take that stance on safety because our growing and vibrant developer community also expects us to do so; it is in their best interest for our platform to invent the future of AR, delight our community and help developers grow their businesses when we build the platforms of the future based on trust and safety.”<\/p>\nBut given the extent to which apps are skirting the rules, it could be more useful if the app stores themselves would integrate these same guidelines into their own app review processes. Or perhaps this is all a sign that regulation, in fact, is needed to protect children and teens from accessing experiences that are either potentially harmful or designed for adults.<\/p>\nAfter all, Snapchat shares the top charts with other apps that cater to a younger, often teenaged, user base — and the rules that apply to it, should apply to anyone.<\/p>\nFor instance, one app eating into the Gen Z market is the newer app called"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/22\/bereal-hype-or-hit-what-to-know-about-the-gen-z-photo-sharing-app-climbing-the-charts\/\">BeReal,<\/a> which prompts users for spontaneous photos. BeReal has now surpassed 10 million cumulative downloads to date, according to estimates from app intelligence firm data.ai (formerly App Annie). Indeed, 3.3 million downloads took place in Q1 alone, and the majority of users in key markets are Gen Z, the firm said.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"gLxtS8EWbs\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/22\/bereal-hype-or-hit-what-to-know-about-the-gen-z-photo-sharing-app-climbing-the-charts\/\">BeReal: Hype or hit? What to know about the Gen Z photo-sharing app climbing the charts<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“BeReal: Hype or hit? What to know about the Gen Z photo-sharing app climbing the charts” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/22\/bereal-hype-or-hit-what-to-know-about-the-gen-z-photo-sharing-app-climbing-the-charts\/embed\/#?secret=Z0i08QtwWM#?secret=gLxtS8EWbs\" data-secret=\"gLxtS8EWbs\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\nAnother app,"https:\/\/apps.apple.com\/us\/app\/livein-livepic-widget\/id1606780589\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">LiveIn<\/a>, caters to Gen Z as well by allowing users to post photos to each others’ homescreens via a widget — a feature BeReal also adopted. It’s now No. 2 on the U.S. App Store’s Top Apps chart, while its rival Locket Widget is No. 24.<\/p>\nThese apps are offering experiences that not only cater to Snapchat’s core demographic, but also features that overlap in some ways with what Snapchat is used for — fun, off-the-cuff photos that aren’t meant to stick around. While Snapchat is"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/21\/snapchat-q1-2022-results\/\">still growing<\/a>, its rivals could expand their own platforms to adopt more Snapchat-like features over time, at which point they could also become a cause for concern if they ventured into similar anonymous Q&A or friend-finding spaces.<\/p>\nFor now, however, these apps present a different type of threat: one that could see Snapchat losing its users’ time and engagement as they try out new ways to connect with friends.<\/p>\nUpdate 5\/17\/22, 4:15 PM ET: Updated to note HMU worked as of yesterday when we tested it. It has since been banned.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"A small handful of Snap Kit platform developers have not yet complied with the new guidelines around anonymous messaging and friend-finding apps announced in March. stribution-system\/","title":{"rendered":"Apple Podcasts gains storage clean-up tools, support for annual subscriptions and a new distribution system"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">As the battle for podcaster talent and distribution heats up among providers, Apple this morning announced the launch of several new features for its Apple Podcasts service, arriving alongside the latest software updates for iPhone, iPad and Mac. Key among these are features for managing podcast storage across devices, tools to enable annual podcast subscriptions and the newly announced Apple Podcasts Delegated Delivery system — a feature that will soon allow creators to more easily distribute their podcasts directly to Apple Podcasts from third-party hosting providers.<\/p>\nApple says this latter addition will save creators time and energy as they’ll be able to authorize their hosting provider to deliver both their free and premium podcast episodes to Apple Podcasts using the provider’s own dashboard. But it also gives Apple a means of competing with services like Spotify’s Anchor, which now provides tools for creation, hosting and distribution across all major listening apps.<\/p>\nStarting this fall, a select number of hosting providers will support the Delegated Delivery system, including Acast, ART19, Blubrry, Buzzsprout, Libsyn, Omny Studio and RSS.com. Apple says these providers represent around 80% of listening for premium content on Apple Podcasts, and more services will be added over time.<\/p>\nThe feature will be available at no additional cost to all creators through Apple Podcasts Connect and creators won’t need a membership to the Apple Podcasts Program to publish their free shows — only to publish premium content.<\/p>\nApple notes additional details about the new system, including educational resources for creators, will be introduced closer to the service’s launch. In the meantime, creators can visit the Hosting Providers page on Apple.com to stay tuned for further updates.<\/p>\nWhile the new distribution technology is top among today’s announcements, another new tool will be welcomed by longtime Apple Podcasts users — particularly those impacted by the app’s more recent bugs.<\/p>\nBecause Apple Podcasts is able to download shows to listeners’ devices, the app can end up consuming a lot of device storage. On iPhones in particular, this can lead to users running out of room for other essential activities — like taking photos or installing new apps and games. This issue was then further"https:\/\/tidbits.com\/2021\/05\/04\/prevent-apples-updated-podcasts-app-from-eating-your-storage\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">complicated<\/a> by the buggy iOS 14.5 and macOS 11.3 releases, which"https:\/\/discussions.apple.com\/thread\/252839042\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">caused unwanted, older episodes<\/a> of shows to be"https:\/\/www.reddit.com\/r\/ios\/comments\/mzat8j\/if_you_use_the_apple_podcast_app_check_the_limit\/gw0g1t1?utm_source=share&utm_medium=web2x&context=3\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">downloaded<\/a>, eating up even more storage.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n"attachment_2319016\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2319016\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2319016\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Annual-Plans-transparent.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"607\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Annual-Plans-transparent.png 3723w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Annual-Plans-transparent.png?resize=150,134 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Annual-Plans-transparent.png?resize=300,268 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Annual-Plans-transparent.png?resize=50,45 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2319016\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Apple<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nWith the launch of iOS 15.5, iPadOS 15.5 and macOS 12.4, Apple is launching new tools to solve the problem of more easily removing a show’s accumulated downloads, potentially freeing up gigs of storage on users’ devices as a result.<\/p>\nFrom the Settings app on iPhone and iPad, users will be able to navigate to Podcasts, then tap on “Automatically Downloaded” to choose how many episodes of shows are downloaded and saved to the device. The menu will allow listeners to choose to download a certain number of recent episodes, like the latest three, five or 10; or users can choose to download all episodes published recently, like in the last seven, 14 or 30 days. Or they can select “All New Episodes” or none by choosing the “Off” option. The latter makes Apple Podcasts function as a streaming-only app, which works for most people who live in areas with reliable cellular connectivity or access to Wi-Fi.<\/p>\nBy default, brand-new Apple Podcasts users will have the last five episodes kept for all episodic shows and all episodes kept for serial shows, the company says. Otherwise, the default will be to keep all new episodes if nothing else is configured.<\/p>\nWhat’s more is when a user selects their preference, the app will then prompt them to remove the automatically downloaded episodes on the device that now no longer meet the newly selected criteria. That means this feature actually works as a bulk clean-up tool for removing a large number of downloads from the device storage. Before, this was a tedious, manual process that could be tackled in different ways. Users could mark shows as played while having the “Remove Played Downloads” setting turned on, or they could"https:\/\/podcasters.apple.com\/support\/1662-automatic-downloads-on-apple-podcasts\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">manually remove<\/a>\u00a0the downloads for a show or individual episodes one by one.<\/p>\nThese new preferences can also be customized at the show level, not just system-wide, for a more personalized experience.<\/p>\nThis new functionality will also be integrated into the iPhone’s recommendations related to cleaning up device storage. From iPhone Storage (under Settings –> General), users will be prompted to keep only the last five episodes and delete older shows if podcast episodes take up more than 15% of their device storage.<\/p>\nThe selected settings carry over to Mac, as well, which gives desktop users the ability to make decisions related to their Mac storage. That means this is the first time listeners can automatically delete old episodes across their devices.<\/p>\n"attachment_2319017\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2319017\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2319017\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Manage-Storage-on-white.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"607\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Manage-Storage-on-white.png 3723w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Manage-Storage-on-white.png?resize=150,134 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Manage-Storage-on-white.png?resize=300,268 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Manage-Storage-on-white.png?resize=768,686 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Manage-Storage-on-white.png?resize=680,607 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Manage-Storage-on-white.png?resize=1536,1372 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Manage-Storage-on-white.png?resize=2048,1830 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Manage-Storage-on-white.png?resize=50,45 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2319017\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Apple<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nFinally, Apple says it’s introducing the option for podcast creators to present annual subscription plans for their premium podcasts alongside their monthly options. These appear when a user taps “Subscribe” or “Try Free” on a show or channel with a subscription. Of note, the annual subscription will now be selected as the default. And, when the annual cost is lower than if the listener paid monthly, the annual plan’s savings will be displayed to the user.<\/p>\nCreators are able to set up their annual subscriptions at price points they choose as they do their monthly subscriptions in Apple Podcasts Connect.<\/p>\nThe subscriptions and new storage features are rolling out with"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">iOS 15.5, iPadOS 15.5 and macOS 12.4. Delegated Delivery will arrive on supported podcast hosting providers later this fall.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\nOther updates to the app in iOS 15.4 include the ability to browse shows by season and filter episodes by status, which will make it easier to find the one users want to play.<\/p>\nThe changes follow a Podcasts app update that introduced"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/20\/apple-unveils-podcast-subscriptions-and-a-redesigned-apple-podcasts-app\/\">a new design<\/a> but also a"https:\/\/tidbits.com\/2021\/05\/04\/prevent-apples-updated-podcasts-app-from-eating-your-storage\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">number<\/a> of"https:\/\/www.fastcompany.com\/90645958\/apple-podcast-app-disaster\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">usability<\/a>"https:\/\/forums.macrumors.com\/threads\/users-despair-at-apple-podcasts-app-after-ios-14-5-update.2293894\/\">issues<\/a> that drove users to third-party podcast apps, including to Apple Podcasts competitor Spotify, which has been heavily investing in the podcast ecosystem. Those departures could limit Apple’s ability to market podcast subscriptions to users, where Apple takes 15%-30% of subscription revenue, similar to the App Store.<\/p>\nAhead of this update, Apple last month introduced three new Apple Podcasts Collections \u2014 Darkside, tbh and Popped \u2014 which focus on true crime, culture and entertainment, respectively, and are available in the U.S. and Canada. It also recently added"https:\/\/podcasters.apple.com\/3142-march-2022-creator-updates\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">support for uploaded MP3 files<\/a> for subscriber audio in addition to WAV and FLAC, tools for getting help with launching subscriptions with"https:\/\/podcasters.apple.com\/support\/3203-jump-start\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Jump-Start<\/a>, and new analytics around"https:\/\/podcasters.apple.com\/3356-new-listening-reports-for-subscriptions\">listening<\/a> and"https:\/\/podcasters.apple.com\/3142-march-2022-creator-updates\">followers<\/a> in Apple Podcasts Connect.<\/p>\n<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"As the battle for podcaster talent and distribution heats up among providers, Apple this morning announced the launch of several new features for its Apple Podcasts service, arriving alongside the latest software updates for iPhone, iPad and Mac. the"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/07\/app-stores-to-see-record-consumer-spend-of-133-billion-in-2021-143-6-billion-new-app-installs\/\">latest<\/a> year-end"https:\/\/www.appannie.com\/en\/insights\/market-data\/2021-end-year-mobile-apps-recap\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reports<\/a>. Global spending across iOS, Google Play and third-party Android app stores in China"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/12\/app-annie-global-app-stores-consumer-spend-up-19-to-170b-in-2021-downloads-grew-5-to-230b\/\">grew 19% in 2021<\/a> to reach $170 billion. Downloads of apps also grew by 5%, reaching 230 billion in 2021, and mobile ad spend grew 23% year over year to reach $295 billion.<\/p>\nToday\u2019s consumers now spend more time in apps than ever before \u2014 even topping the time they spend watching TV, in some cases. The average American watches 3.1 hours of TV per day, for example, but in 2021, they spent 4.1 hours on their mobile device. And they\u2019re not even the world\u2019s heaviest mobile users. In markets like Brazil, Indonesia and South Korea, users surpassed five hours per day in mobile apps in 2021.<\/p>\nApps aren\u2019t just a way to pass idle hours, either. They can grow to become huge businesses. In 2021, 233 apps and games"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/12\/app-annie-global-app-stores-consumer-spend-up-19-to-170b-in-2021-downloads-grew-5-to-230b\/\">generated over $100 million<\/a> in consumer spend, and 13 topped $1 billion in revenue. This was up 20% from 2020, when 193 apps and games topped $100 million in annual consumer spend, and just eight apps topped $1 billion.<\/p>\nThis Week in Apps offers a way to keep up with this fast-moving industry in one place, with the latest from the world of apps, including news, updates, startup fundings, mergers and acquisitions, and suggestions about new apps to try, too.<\/p>\nDo you want This Week in Apps in your inbox every Saturday? But did we have fun?<\/p>\nIt’s a shame Google’s big developer event was still largely hybrid — save for select invitees (Google’s partners), the event was only streamed. The keynotes are held at an outdoor amphitheater so the COVID-era rule is starting to not make sense. Concerts are open and tech employees are being shuffled back to the office, but outdoor tech events are still closed, I guess? Unfortunately, this decision impacts those not fortunate enough to make the guest list at these real-world happenings that offer networking opportunities and chances to engage directly with Google employees. At least Apple turned WWDC into a"https:\/\/www.engadget.com\/apple-invites-in-person-wwdc-2022-event-072132309.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">random lottery<\/a>, or so it says. After all, the keynotes are not the main reason developers go to these things.<\/p>\nIn any event, Google’s event sort of felt like an off-year, where some of the biggest hardware announcements had no exact ship dates, beyond “fall” or “next year” or “who knows?!” During the keynote, Google unveiled a lower-cost"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/googles-budget-pixel-6a-arrives-july-28-for-449\/\">Pixel 6a phone<\/a> and new"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-finally-brings-noise-cancellation-to-pixel-buds\/\">Pixel Buds<\/a>, both coming this summer, and the big news of"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/googles-pixel-watch-arrives-this-fall\/\">its first smartwatch<\/a>, arriving this fall. But other announcements were just teased, like the Tensor-powered"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-offers-a-peek-at-the-pixel-7\/\">Pixel 7<\/a>, due this fall; a new Android tablet (the"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-will-release-a-pixel-tablet-in-2023\/\">Pixel tablet<\/a>) for 2023; and"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-glasss-successor-teased-at-i-o\/\">Google’s concept for AR glasses<\/a>, with a ship date of IDK MAYBE ONE DAY.<\/p>\nIn terms of Android developer news, there was still quite a bit:<\/p>\n\nPlay Store:<\/strong>\u00a0"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-play-targets-emerging-markets-with-prepaid-app-subscriptions-and-more\/\">Highlights include<\/a> prepaid app subscriptions, new “ultra-low” price points (e.g. for emerging markets or tipping), better ways of bundling subscriptions and offers, and more. On the storefront itself,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-play-adopts-app-store-like-features-including-in-app-events-and-custom-product-pages\/\">Google Play added in-app events and custom product pages<\/a>, among other things.<\/li>\nDev tools:<\/strong>"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-updates-its-firebase-backend-as-a-service-to-make-app-development-faster\/\">Updated Firebase<\/a> backend-as-a-service for faster app development;"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/googles-flutter-3-adds-support-for-macos-and-linux-desktop-apps\/\">Flutter 3<\/a> added support for macOS and Linux desktop apps;"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/googles-android-studio-ide-gets-live-edits-to-speed-up-development-cycles\/\">Android Studio gained live edits<\/a> to speed up dev cycles; a"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-and-samsung-team-up-to-make-sharing-data-between-health-and-fitness-apps-easier\/\">Samsung partnership<\/a> for easier data sharing between health and fitness apps; and a new"https:\/\/developers.googleblog.com\/2022\/05\/Make-the-world-your-canvas-ARCore-Geospatial-API.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">ARCore Geospational API<\/a>, based on Google Visual Positioning System and Street View images, that lets developers anchor content via GPS, saving resources by not having to scan the physical space. (More below).<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nPlus Google"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/google-io-2022\/\">announced other updates<\/a>, including a new"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-launches-google-wallet\/\">Google Wallet app<\/a>, new"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-details-its-latest-language-model-and-ai-test-kitchen-a-showcase-for-ai-research\/\"> AI models<\/a> (e.g. LaMDA 2), a new"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-maps-challenges-apples-3d-mode-with-a-new-immersive-view-for-cities\/\">“immersive” mode on Google Maps<\/a>, ad personalization"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-will-allow-users-control-how-ads-are-personalized-on-search-youtube-and-elsewhere-with-new-tool\/\">tools<\/a>, Google Cloud"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-launches-a-9-exaflop-cluster-of-cloud-tpu-v4-pods-into-public-preview\/\">updates<\/a>,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-brings-phishing-detection-to-docs-sheets-and-slides-along-with-other-privacy-and-security-updates\/\">security<\/a> tools,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-makes-it-easier-to-chat-with-its-assistant\/\">Assistant features<\/a> and more.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"xAljjFnCs7\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/googles-new-multisearch-features-hint-towards-an-ar-glasses-future\/\">Google’s new ‘multisearch’ features hint toward an AR glasses future<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Google’s new ‘multisearch’ features hint toward an AR glasses future” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/googles-new-multisearch-features-hint-towards-an-ar-glasses-future\/embed\/#?secret=PPKpGPQd5P#?secret=xAljjFnCs7\" data-secret=\"xAljjFnCs7\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\nARCore Geospatial API<\/h3>\nA couple of interesting things at I\/O did hint toward Google’s longer-term vision for AR, starting with"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/googles-new-multisearch-features-hint-towards-an-ar-glasses-future\/\">its latest mulitsearch advances.<\/a> Announced"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/07\/googles-multisearch-search-using-text-images\/\">earlier<\/a> this year, multisearch lets users combine images and text into a single Google Search query to tackle the sorts of searches that a text search alone could struggle with, or to aid with shopping purchases. But the tech could one day serve to help users scan items in the real world. For starters, Google said users can now scan real-world items and then add “near me” to their query to find a nearby retail store that carries the item in question.<\/p>\nBut more interestingly, Google said one day users will be able to pan their camera around to learn about multiple objects within that wider scene. The company suggested the feature could be used to scan the shelves at a bookstore, then see helpful several insights overlaid in front of you.<\/p>\n"attachment_2316776\" style=\"width: 690px\" come out and say that.<\/p>\n\u201cThere are 8 billion visual searches on Google with Lens every single month now and that number is three times the size that it was just a year ago,\u201d said Nick And what we\u2019re trying to do now is lean into the use cases and identify where this is most useful,\u201d he said. \u201cI think as we think about the future of search, visual search is definitely a key part of that.\u201d<\/p>\nToday, many developers are trying out AR experiences in their smartphone apps wondering how consumers will react to the new features. At I\/O, Google shared how it sees use cases for AR. These ranged from scanning the world in front of you and augmenting it with information to indoor navigation to playing games.
"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-maps-challenges-apples-3d-mode-with-a-new-immersive-view-for-cities\/\">Google presented several experiences<\/a> built by the new ARCore Geospatial API’s early adopters, which included AR gaming, navigation aids that helped concert-goers find their seats, as well as new tools offered by"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/bird-lime-to-use-googles-arcore-to-power-scooter-parking-solution\/\">Bird and Lime to help people geolocate<\/a> where to park their scooters and e-bikes with “less than a meter accuracy.”<\/p>\nThese tools are in the hands of Android and iOS app developers, but one day, the screen developers are building for may no longer be only the rectangular smartphone — but eyewear. (On that note,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/mark-zuckerberg-shows-off-metas-next-headset-kind-of\/\">Meta tried to steal the spotlight<\/a> with a tease of its mixed reality glasses, but what’s there to say about a pixelated Zuck video?)<\/p>\nBut AR glasses are still a bet that the future generation wants a world with ever more personal tech, where tech becomes a further part of the human condition and experience, rather than the handheld tool it is today. That vision also implies the Big Tech backlash we’re experiencing today will come to an end, and people will agree to put Google or Facebookon their face.<\/em> I mean,<\/em> even in “Star Trek” they still used tablets, you know?<\/p>\nElon pauses Twitter deal…well, not really…Oh, who knows!!<\/h3>\n"attachment_2309907\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2309907\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2309907\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/elon-musk-twitter.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"Elon Musk icon over twitter icons\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/elon-musk-twitter.jpg 3200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/elon-musk-twitter.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/elon-musk-twitter.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/elon-musk-twitter.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/elon-musk-twitter.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/elon-musk-twitter.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/elon-musk-twitter.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/elon-musk-twitter.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2309907\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Bryce Durbin \/ TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nElon’s trolling. Crypto apps are all feeling the impacts and Binance"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/binance-halts-luna-and-ust-trading-across-most-of-its-spot-pairs-following-meltdown\/\">announced<\/a> it was indefinitely halting trading of Terraform Labs\u2019 Terra (Luna) and TerraUSD (UST) tokens.<\/li>\nCoinbase’s decline has mirrored the drop in Bitcoin prices, with its market cap falling to $12.98 billion from a $75 billion+ peak in 2021<\/strong> per"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2022-05-12\/coinbase-melts-down-even-as-wall-street-is-bullish-on-prospects\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bloomberg<\/a>. At launch, supported blockchains include Ethereum and Polygon, with support for Flow and Solana coming soon. Third-party wallets compatible for use at launch include Rainbow, MetaMask and Trust Wallet, with Coinbase, Dapper and Phantom coming soon.<\/li>\nTikTok"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/09\/tiktok-friends-tab-replacing-discover-tab\/\">rolled out a Friends tab<\/a> for watching videos from people you know, replacing the Discover tab in the app<\/strong>. Who said we wanted to hang out with friends on TikTok?! The app had been pushing people to upload their contacts to the app for weeks prior to the move.<\/li>\nTikTok and Foursquare"https:\/\/www.adweek.com\/programmatic\/tiktok-foursquare-expand-partnership-to-include-foursquare-attribution\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">expanded a partnership<\/a> to include Foursquare Attribution<\/strong>. The deal gives advertisers access to conversion insights from the measurement product Foursquare Attribution, which helps track how ads drive people into brick-and-mortar stores.<\/li>\nFacebook said it’s"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/09\/facebook-to-shutter-its-nearby-friends-service-having-lost-the-friend-finding-market\/\">shuttering its Nearby Friends service<\/a> after eight years<\/strong>. The closure will come on May 31, along with Weather Alerts, location history and background location, all of which are also being discontinued.<\/li>\nFour U.S. representatives"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/russia-ukraine-social-media-war-crimes-congress\/\">sent letters<\/a> to the CEOs of Meta, TikTok, YouTube and Twitter<\/strong> asking them to archive any content uploaded to their platforms that could be used as evidence of Russian war crimes.<\/li>\nA parent is"https:\/\/www.businessinsider.com\/tiktok-sued-by-mother-of-girl-died-in-choking-challenge-2022-5\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">suing TikTok<\/a> <\/strong>alleging her child died after repeating the blackout challenge she saw on the app.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nDating<\/h3>\n\nTinder parent"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/09\/match-group-google-lawsuit-google-play\/\">Match Group sued Google<\/a><\/strong> saying its move to force developers to shift to the Google billing system is an abuse of power. Google"https:\/\/blog.google\/outreach-initiatives\/public-policy\/setting-the-record-straight-on-match-groups-cynical-campaign-against-google-play\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">dismissed<\/a> the claim saying Match just wanted to avoid paying its fair share.<\/li>\nBumble beat on its Q1 earnings estimates with revenue of $211.2 million up 24% year-over-year<\/strong>, and paying users up 7% year-over-year to 3 million. The"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2022-05-11\/bumble-surges-as-revenue-beats-estimates-on-new-paying-users\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stock jumped 17%<\/a> in extended trading on the news.<\/li>\nGrindr"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2022-05-09\/grindr-to-go-public-through-tiga-spac-at-2-1-billion-valuation\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">agreed to go public via a SPAC merger<\/a> at a $2.1 billion valuation including debt<\/strong>. The move will raise ~$384 million. The dating app had $147 million revenue in 2021, up 30% year-over-year.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nMessaging<\/h3>\n\nWhatsApp"https:\/\/wabetainfo.com\/whatsapp-is-rolling-out-the-ability-to-add-up-to-512-people-to-groups\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">rolled out<\/a> Message Reactions<\/strong>, support for sharing files up to 2GB in size, and the ability to add up to 512 people to a group.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nStreaming & In its filing, Apple expressed serious concerns, saying it would have to redesign the iPhone to benefit the developers who wanted to remove the App Store’s consumer protection features.<\/li>\nU.S. Senator Michael Bennet"https:\/\/www.engadget.com\/us-lawmaker-commission-oversee-tech-companies-051444592.html?src=rss\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">introduced<\/a> the Digital Platform Commission Act, in an effort to establish a federal watchdog specifically for overseeing Big Tech companies.<\/strong> He argues that the government doesn’t have the tech expertise to make some of the decisions, and suggests the federal body should be staffed with experts in digital fields.
