Deal terms were not disclosed, but the full six-person team will now join Snap and remain in Toronto.<\/p>\n\ud83d\udcb0 Travel insurance startup Faye"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/faye-hopes-to-do-for-travel-insurance-what-lemonade-did-for-general-insurance\/\">raised $8 million<\/a> in a seed funding round<\/strong> led by Viola Ventures and F2 Venture Capital. The startup covers trips, health, belongings and pets via an app that sends alerts, offers 24\/7customer support and enables digital claims filing, as well as electronic transfers of reimbursements to its Faye Wallet.<\/p>\n\ud83d\udcb0 Creator app Fanhouse"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/fanhouse-creator-monetization-rosie-nguyen\/\">raised $20 million<\/a> in Series A funding from Andreessen Horowitz<\/strong> for its platform that allows creators to connect directly with their community and generate revenue. Each fan views content that’s watermarked uniquely for them, to help prevent leaks. The app is nearing $10 million-plus in creator payouts after two years, it said.<\/p>\n\ud83d\udcb0 Payments infrastructure provider Paddle, which wants to offer a third-party solution to app developers if stores open up,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/09\/paddle-saas-series-d\/\">raised $200 million<\/a> in Series D funding<\/strong> led by KKR. The deal values the business, which now has 3,000 software customers, at $1.4 billion.<\/p>\n\ud83d\udcb0 <\/strong>Altro, an app that helps you build credit through everyday recurring payments and subscriptions,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/jayz-backed-altro-just-raised-18m-to-help-you-build-credit-just-by-paying-for-your-netflix-subscription\/\">raised $18 million<\/a> in a Series A funding<\/strong> round led by Pendulum. musk-deal\/","title":{"rendered":"Top Twitter execs, including heads of revenue and consumer products, are out following Musk deal"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Twitter GM of Consumer, Keyvon Beykpour,"https:\/\/twitter.com\/kayvz\/status\/1524787800863744002\">announced<\/a> today he will be leaving the company after seven years. Beykpour first joined the social media platform by way of its acquisition of Periscope, which he founded. He said in a tweet he was asked to leave by"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/29\/daily-crunch-twitter-ceo-jack-dorsey-steps-down-board-moves-cto-parag-agrawal-to-top-spot\/\">current<\/a> CEO Parag Agrawal, who wants to take the team in another direction.
"https:\/\/twitter.com\/boo\">Bruce Falck<\/a>, Twitter’s revenue product lead, is also departing, Twitter confirmed to TechCrunch.<\/p>\nA Twitter spokesperson said its VP of Consumer Products Jay Sullivan will now become the new GM of Bluebird and interim GM of Goldbird.<\/p>\nIn addition, the company confirmed it’s undergoing a hiring freeze — which is not uncommon following M&A deals.<\/p>\n“Effective this week, we are pausing most hiring and backfills, except for business-critical roles. We are also pulling back on non-labor costs to ensure we are being responsible and efficient,” the spokesperson said.<\/p>\nThe company had no further comment on the changes.<\/p>\n“The truth is that this isn\u2019t how and when I imagined leaving Twitter, and this wasn\u2019t my decision,”"https:\/\/twitter.com\/kayvz\/status\/1524787800863744002\">wrote<\/a> Beykpour on Twitter. The exec was on paternity leave at the time he received the news, he noted. “While I\u2019m disappointed, I take solace in a few things: I am INSANELY proud of what our collective team achieved over the last few years, and my own contribution to this journey,” Beykpour added before reeling off accomplishments that took place under his leadership.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Interrupting my paternity leave to share some final"https:\/\/twitter.com\/Twitter?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@twitter<\/a>-related news: I\u2019m leaving the company after over 7 years.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n— Kayvon Beykpour (@kayvz)"https:\/\/twitter.com\/kayvz\/status\/1524787800863744002?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">May 12, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\nAfter joining Twitter by way of the live video app Periscope in July 2018, Beykpour become Twitter’s head of Consumer Product. He then moved up to GM, Consumer in December 2021 — an elevated role that saw him leading all teams across Product, Engineering, Design, Research and Customer Service & Operations teams that worked on Twitter’s consumer apps.<\/p>\nIn his tweets, Beykpour noted Twitter’s DAU (daily active users) grew by over 87% since the second quarter of 2018 and his team has since shipped a variety of products. Notably, his team is behind the surge in product innovation Twitter had seen in recent months that gave birth to new product concepts like its live audio chat rooms, Twitter Spaces, as well as Communities, Topics, Creator Tools, Safety controls and more. These products began to ship at a much faster pace than any time over the past decade, said Beykpour.<\/p>\nHe went on to thank his team and fellow employees, specifically calling out Jay Sullivan, the former Meta product director who"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/in\/sullivanjay\/\">joined<\/a> the company last year and"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/technology\/twitter-names-new-leaders-consumer-unit-push-add-users-2022-03-11\/\">became<\/a> Twitter’s VP of Consumer Products; as well as former Twitter CEO Dick Costolo who brought Persicope to Twitter in the first place; and Twitter’s most recent CEO before Agrawal, Jack Dorsey; among others.<\/p>\nFalck, meanwhile, took to Twitter to thank the teams and partners he’s worked with over the past five years.<\/p>\n“We were able to achieve the results we did through your hard work – – quarterly revenue does not lie. Google it,” he tweeted.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n"en\" dir=\"ltr\">I wanted to take a moment to thank all the teams and partners I\u2019ve been lucky enough to work with during the past 5 years. Building and running these businesses is a team sport<\/p>\n— bruce.falck() \ud83e\udd97 (@boo)"https:\/\/twitter.com\/boo\/status\/1524795027125198852?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">May 12, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\nThe departure follows Tesla and SpaceX exec Elon Musk’s decision to acquire Twitter and take it in a direction that’s focused more on “free speech.” Musk has other"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/29\/elon-musk-lined-up-twitter-ceo-ideas-monetizing-tweets\/\">specific plans<\/a> for Twitter products, he’s said, like verifying users who pay for Twitter Blue subscriptions, charging for embedded tweets and other changes designed to grow Twitter revenue and users. It’s not clear what that means for all the products Beykpour’s team had spearheaded, however.<\/p>\nAgrawal had begun"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/29\/daily-crunch-twitter-ceo-jack-dorsey-steps-down-board-moves-cto-parag-agrawal-to-top-spot\/\">restructuring<\/a> the Twitter team back in December, after taking over the role formerly held by Dorsey. At the time, Twitter lost its Chief Design Officer Dantley Davis, who joined the company in 2019, and its Head of Engineering Michael Montano, who joined in 2011. Shortly after,"https:\/\/www.protocol.com\/bulletins\/twitter-security-heads-leaving-shakeup\">Twitter lost two more leaders<\/a>, chief information security officer, Rinki Sethi, and head of Security, Peiter Zatko (Mudge).<\/p>\nIt wouldn’t be surprising to see further changes to Twitter’s organization and its leadership in the days to come.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Twitter GM of Consumer, Keyvon Beykpour, announced today he will be leaving the company after seven years. agrawal","slug":"parag-agrawal","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576957053"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576957053"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576957053"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576957053"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576957053"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2316479,"date":"2022-05-12T09:00:25","date_gmt":"2022-05-12T16:00:25","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2316479"},"modified":"2022-05-12T12:24:20","modified_gmt":"2022-05-12T19:24:20","slug":"google-tv-app-to-add-casting-as-android-tv-ecosystem-grows-to-110m-monthly-active-devices","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/google-tv-app-to-add-casting-as-android-tv-ecosystem-grows-to-110m-monthly-active-devices\/","title":{"rendered":"Google TV app to add casting as Android TV ecosystem grows to 110M monthly active devices"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Following last year’s"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/27\/google-tv-mobile-app-redesign-adds-new-services-and-recommendations\/\">makeover of the Google TV app<\/a>, which added features like movie and TV recommendations, critics’ scores and more, the company today announced at its Google I\/O developer conference that, later this year, users will be able to cast TV shows and movies directly from their Android phone or tablet to their TV. The company additionally offered updated metrics related to its Android OS’ growing footprint and introduced new Android OS developer tools.<\/p>\nGoogle has been working to overhaul its connected TV experience and the companion app since 2020, when it first"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/09\/30\/the-new-chromecast-adds-a-remote-and-the-new-google-tv-interface-for-49\/\">introduced<\/a> the"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/23\/google-moving-movies-tv-tab-play-store-google-tv\/\">new Google TV interface<\/a> for its Chromecast streaming devices. It also applied the Google TV name to the app that was previously known as the Google Play Movies & TV app. Earlier this year, Google also"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/23\/google-moving-movies-tv-tab-play-store-google-tv\/\">removed the “Movies & TV” section<\/a> from the Play Store, noting the Google TV app would be the centralized place to buy, rent and watch movies and TV shows on mobile devices.<\/p>\nThe company didn’t provide additional details about its plans to add support for casting to the app, saying those would come closer to launch. But in a photo Google provided, it showed at least one of the supported apps is NBCU’s Peacock.<\/p>\n"attachment_2316535\" style=\"width: 1177px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2316535\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2316535 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Cast-from-Google-TV-app.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"1167\" height=\"773\" \/>"caption-attachment-2316535\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Google<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nAs part of its announcements, the company also offered a few updates on the Android TV ecosystem, noting there are now 110 million monthly active devices on Android TV OS, including Google TV. That’s up from the"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/18\/android-tv-os-reaches-80m-monthly-active-devices-adds-new-features\/\">80 million monthly active devices<\/a> figure Google announced at last year’s Google I\/O event.<\/p>\nIt also said the Android TV OS now offers over 10,000 apps.<\/p>\nOf course, the Android TV OS is not a direct equivalent to something like Roku or Amazon Fire TV, as it’s not only used on the company’s first-party devices, like Chromecast. Instead, Google’s strategy is to license its platform to partners, including TV OEMs and pay-TV operators worldwide. Currently, there are over 300 partners using the platform, including seven out of the 10 largest TV OEMs, Google said.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nBut Google’s 110 million active devices figure can’t be directly compared with the metrics shared by rivals Roku and Amazon.<\/p>\nAndroid TV OS figures are actually calculated by counting the number of devices that were actively used in a month \u2014 which means a user with multiple devices could have those devices counted separately, but a family with multiple people watching on one device would be counted once.<\/p>\nRoku and Amazon define monthly active users as “accounts” that have been active during the month. That means, even if that account streams on several different devices during the time period, it would only be counted once. If Roku or Amazon were to calculate active devices as Google is doing, their numbers would be higher.<\/p>\nIn December 2020, Amazon said Fire TV had topped"https:\/\/advertising.amazon.com\/blog\/amazon-advertisers-can-now-reach-up-to-50m-monthly-active-users-on-fire-tv\">50 million<\/a> monthly active users — a number still"https:\/\/advertising.amazon.com\/solutions\/products\/video-ads?ref_=a20m_us_hnav_p_va\">referenced<\/a> today on its Amazon Ads website.\u00a0This January, Amazon also noted it had sold"https:\/\/variety.com\/2022\/digital\/news\/amazon-fire-tv-150-million-sold-1235147080\/\">more than 150 million<\/a> Fire TV devices to bring its metrics more in line with Google’s device claims. Roku, meanwhile, said during it had ended 2021"https:\/\/variety.com\/2022\/digital\/news\/roku-q1-2022-streaming-slowdown-1235243519\/\">with 60.1 million<\/a> active accounts. It updated that figure to 61.3 million accounts in Q1 2022.\u00a0 It doesn’t count active devices.<\/p>\n"attachment_2316533\" style=\"width: 1290px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2316533\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2316533 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Picture-in-Picture.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1280\" height=\"720\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Picture-in-Picture.png 1280w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Picture-in-Picture.png?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Picture-in-Picture.png?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Picture-in-Picture.png?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Picture-in-Picture.png?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Picture-in-Picture.png?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1280px) 100vw, 1280px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2316533\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Google<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nGoogle also highlighted several developer features and tools on Android 13 related to its Android TV efforts. The tools are focused on performance and quality, accessibilty and multitasking, Google said, and include:<\/p>\n\nAudioManager:<\/strong> This allows apps to anticipate audio routes and precisely understand which playback mode is available.<\/li>\nMediaSession<\/strong>: Integration with app allows Android TV to react to HDMI state changes to save power and signal content to be paused.<\/li>\nInputDevice API:<\/strong> Added support for different keyboard layouts. (For game developers, added support for different layouts of physical keyboards, such as QWERTZ and AZERTY keyboards.)<\/li>\nSystemwide accessibility preference<\/strong>: Allow users to enable audio descriptions across apps.<\/li>\nPicture-in-picture (PIP) API:<\/strong> PIP on the TV supports an expanded mode to show videos from a group call and a docked mode to avoid overlaying content to other apps.<\/li>\nKeep-clear API:<\/strong> Prevents overlay from concealing important content in full-screen apps.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\nThe picture-in-picture API is particularly interesting as it could introduce more co-watching functionality across the Android TV ecosystem, following"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/07\/apple-introduces-shareplay-for-co-watching-streaming-and-screen-sharing-over-facetime\/\">Apple’s introduction of SharePlay,<\/a> which allows co-watching over FaceTime across platforms, including Apple TV.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Following last year’s makeover of the Google TV app, which added features like movie and TV recommendations, critics’ scores and more, the company today announced at its Google I\/O developer conference that, later this year, users will be able to cast TV shows and movies directly from their Android phone or tablet to their TV. Play","slug":"google-play","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/32740565"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=32740565"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=32740565"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=32740565"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=32740565"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2317594,"date":"2022-05-12T08:38:24","date_gmt":"2022-05-12T15:38:24","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2317594"},"modified":"2022-05-12T12:57:40","modified_gmt":"2022-05-12T19:57:40","slug":"amazons-alexa-app-now-asks-customers-to-scan-their-shopping-receipts-for-cashback-rewards","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/amazons-alexa-app-now-asks-customers-to-scan-their-shopping-receipts-for-cashback-rewards\/","title":{"rendered":"Amazon’s Alexa app feature lets customers option to scan their shopping receipts for cashback rewards"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">It’s been said that"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/08\/06\/surprise-no-one-buys-things-via-alexa\/\">no one uses Alexa<\/a> for voice-based shopping. But retail giant still sees the potential for Alexa as a shopping companion — just in a different way. That’s why this month the company quietly rolled out a new feature designed to boost consumers’ use of Alexa’s Shopping Lists:"https:\/\/www.amazon.com\/b?node=23869270011&tag=aftvn-20\">cashback offers<\/a>.<\/p>\nThe company confirmed to TechCrunch it introduced “"https:\/\/www.amazon.com\/b?node=23869270011&tag=aftvn-20\">Alexa Shopping List Savings<\/a>,” which puts rebate offers from brands and manufacturers directly into consumers’ hands through the Alexa app, its mobile companion app for Echo device owners. The company says the offers will be displayed in the Alexa Shopping List section within the app and then can be used across retail stores nationwide to help customers save money.<\/p>\nTo use the feature, you’d first select the offers of interest and activate them in the app, then visit your favorite grocery store, drug store, or chain store to buy the product, the Amazon website explains in an FAQ. The details about the offers around how they can be applied are also available in the app, Amazon notes. When you’ve completed your purchase, shoppers claim their rebate by taking a photo of the store receipt that shows the store’s name, location, date and time of purchases, product price and total, then submit it to Amazon through the app. Customers also have to scan the barcode on the product itself to complete the process.<\/p>\nAmazon will send the rebate to the customer via their Amazon Gift Card account. This process may take up to a week but typically takes just 24-48 hours, Amazon says. The Gift Card balance can be used to shop across tens of millions of eligible products on Amazon.<\/p>\n"attachment_2317634\" style=\"width: 1510px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2317634\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2317634 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/amazon-alexa-offers.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1594\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/amazon-alexa-offers.png 1500w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/amazon-alexa-offers.png?resize=141,150 141w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/amazon-alexa-offers.png?resize=282,300 282w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/amazon-alexa-offers.png?resize=768,816 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/amazon-alexa-offers.png?resize=640,680 640w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/amazon-alexa-offers.png?resize=1445,1536 1445w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/amazon-alexa-offers.png?resize=47,50 47w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1500px) 100vw, 1500px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2317634\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Amazon<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nAs you may expect, this system provides Amazon with a treasure trove of customer shopping data beyond just the offers customers were interested in and were redeeming.<\/p>\nThe website notes that by choosing to participate in the Alexa Shopping List Savings program, customers are agreeing to share their personal information and data with Amazon:<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n\u2026 we will get any information you provide, including receipt images and information we may extract from those receipts, and the offers you activate. You understand and acknowledge that your personal information may be shared with Amazon\u2019s service providers.<\/p><\/blockquote>\nThe data will be used and shared per Amazon’s privacy policy"https:\/\/www.amazon.com\/gp\/help\/customer\/display.html?nodeId=468496&ref_=footer_privacy\">terms,<\/a> the site notes. Further details were not provided.<\/p>\nBroadly, this business model is not unique to Amazon. Other apps offer similar tools to turn customers’ retail store receipts into “free” gift cards. (They’re not really free — you paid with your data!) For instance, apps like Fetch Rewards, Ibotta, Checkout51 and others make money through affiliate commissions, through the resale of customers’ anonymized data or both, then share some of that revenue back with the customer in the form of cash back or gift cards.<\/p>\nLike rival apps, Amazon’s offers tend to be the same sort of grocery rewards you’d see elsewhere. This includes consumer packaged goods, health and beauty items, baby items, canned food and more — not fresh groceries or other retail categories, like electronics or apparel.<\/p>\nOf course, some people don’t mind sharing their data with businesses in exchange for rewards or cash back — top apps like Fetch and Ibotta have millions of users, in fact. But consumers should be aware that Amazon’s privacy policy makes no promises of anonymizing any data nor does it explain in detail exactly how this data will be put to use.<\/p>\nThe feature is live in the Amazon Alexa mobile app today.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"It’s been said that no one uses Alexa for voice-based shopping. But retail giant still sees the potential for Alexa as a shopping companion — just in a different way. That’s why this month the company quietly rolled out a new feature designed to boost consumers’ use of Alexa’s Shopping Lists: cashback offers. snaps up database developer KeyDB to make its infrastructure more snappy"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">As Snapchat’s app"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/21\/snapchat-q1-2022-results\/\">continues<\/a> to grow, the company is turning to the open source community to help further improve its technology infrastructure. This morning, Snap announced it’s acquiring Toronto-based"https:\/\/docs.keydb.dev\/docs\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">KeyDB<\/a>, the developer of an open source, high-performance database, for an undisclosed sum.<\/p>\nThe startup’s six-person team, including its co-founders John Sully and Ben Schermel, will join Snap’s infrastructure team following the deal’s close, and will work to improve Snap’s caching technology and its sizable engineering workloads, the company says.<\/p>\nA"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/24\/here-are-the-98-companies-from-y-combinators-summer-2020-demo-day-1\/\">Y Combinator-backed<\/a> startup, KeyDB touted its solution as being a faster alternative to Redis, offering a focus on things like multithreading, memory efficiency and high throughput. For Snap, it sees the advantage in bringing the technology — and the team’s expertise — in-house to help the company reduce its operational costs across teams and to free up engineering bandwidth. This also allows Snap to focus more on building out other core Snapchat experiences, the company said.<\/p>\nA Snap spokesperson told TechCrunch that KeyDB’s technology will be of significant use across all of Snap, including its monetization and Spotlight platforms. The latter is Snapchat’s short-form video product and a rival to TikTok, which is now a key part of Snap’s business.<\/p>\nKeyDB’s multithreaded database utilizes Redis data structures, flash storage and replication, and runs at Snap scale, the company noted. It’s also an open source project that has a large community, with more than 3 million public downloads.<\/p>\nFortunately for other engineers, Snap says it will continue the open source project and will also open source KeyDB’s Pro and Enterprise offerings following the acquisition. This will allow the company to continue to benefit from the broader community contributions, we’re told, but will also help Snap to better establish its own presence within the open source community and establish relationships with more developers.<\/p>\nPlus, as Snap’s engineers merge their own internal improvements into the KeyDB project, the company believes it will be able to help solve challenges across the broader community.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nGoing forward, visitors to the"https:\/\/github.com\/EQ-Alpha\/KeyDB\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">KeyDB GitHub repository<\/a> will be redirected to the"https:\/\/github.com\/Snapchat\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">"il\">Snap<\/span> GitHub repository<\/a>.<\/p>\nThe KeyDB team, meanwhile, will continue to work from Toronto, where Snap already has a sizable office that includes, among others, its Bitmoji team.<\/p>\nSnap has been fairly acquisitive over the past year or so, with many of its recent mergers and acquisitions being focused on underlying technologies. In 2021, for instance, Snap bought 3D mapping developer"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/26\/snap-has-acquired-pixel8earth-a-3d-mapping-developer-for-7-6m\/\"> Pixel8earth for $7.6 million<\/a>,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/17\/snap-is-taking-a-significant-step-into-fashion-e-commerce-with-its-acquisition-of-fit-analytics\/\">fitting technology startup Fit Analytics<\/a> for"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/23\/filing-snap-paid-124m-for-fit-analytics-as-it-gears-up-for-a-bigger-e-commerce-push\/\">$124 million<\/a>, location data startup"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/11\/snap-acquires-streetcred\/\">StreetCred<\/a>, mind-controlled"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/23\/snap-buys-mind-controlled-headband-maker-nextmind\/\">headband maker NextMind<\/a> and an AR startup to power Spectacles,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/21\/snap-acquires-ar-startup-waveoptics-which-provides-tech-for-spectacles-for-over-500m\/\">WaveOptics, <\/a>for"https:\/\/www.sec.gov\/ix?doc=\/Archives\/edgar\/data\/1564408\/000156459022003868\/snap-10k_20211231.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$541.8+ million<\/a>.<\/p>\nThe company had"https:\/\/www.sec.gov\/ix?doc=\/Archives\/edgar\/data\/1564408\/000156459022003868\/snap-10k_20211231.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">disclosed<\/a> the prices for FitAnalytics and WaveOptics in an SEC filing due to their size, but said all 2021 acquisitions in aggregate only totaled $266.1 million. The company would not discuss KeyDB’s price, but Crunchbase"https:\/\/www.crunchbase.com\/funding_round\/eq-alpha-technology-ltd-seed--c7bc3486\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reports<\/a> the company was seed-funded with $1.3 million.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"As Snapchat’s app continues to grow, the company is turning to the open source community to help further improve its technology infrastructure. The startup’s six-person team, including its co-founders John Sully and Ben Schermel, will inc","slug":"snap-inc","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449553840"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449553840"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449553840"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449553840"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449553840"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2315456,"date":"2022-05-11T13:00:44","date_gmt":"2022-05-11T20:00:44","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2315456"},"modified":"2022-05-11T15:24:45","modified_gmt":"2022-05-11T22:24:45","slug":"google-play-targets-emerging-markets-with-prepaid-app-subscriptions-and-more","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-play-targets-emerging-markets-with-prepaid-app-subscriptions-and-more\/","title":{"rendered":"Google Play targets emerging markets with prepaid app subscriptions and more"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">At the Google I\/O developer conference today, the company introduced several changes designed to make it easier for Android app developers to generate revenue via subscriptions, particularly when trying to reach users in emerging markets. Most notably, the company said it will"https:\/\/android-developers.googleblog.com\/2022\/05\/new-ways-to-sell-subscriptions-on-google-play.html\">now allow developers<\/a> to offer users the ability to subscribe via prepaid plans that essentially provide access to an app and its services for fixed amount of time the developer sets.<\/p>\nThe users would then be able to buy top-ups in the app when their subscription ran out and they had the funds to continue. Google said the feature would make sense in regions where pay-as-you-go cellular plans are standard. In those markets, consumers are already used to the prepaid model, so extending it to apps could help to boost developers’ subscription revenues. However, prepaid subscriptions could also help to target other use cases as well — like subscription-adverse customers who are hesitant to get locked into ongoing charges and who want more control over when and how much they’re spending on their mobile apps.<\/p>\nGoogle also"https:\/\/android-developers.googleblog.com\/2022\/05\/new-ways-to-sell-subscriptions-on-google-play.html\">announced<\/a> expanded pricing options with the launch of “ultra-low” price points to reach users in emerging markets.<\/p>\nLast March, Google had reduced the minimum price limit for products in more than 20 markets across Latin America, Europe, the Middle East, Africa and Asia-Pacific, allowing developers to drop prices down to as low as 10 to 30 cents (USD). At the time, the company explained these “sub-dollar prices” would allow developers to reach new potential buyers by adjusting pricing to “better reflect local purchasing power and demand.”<\/p>\nNow, Google says developers can drop prices to as low as 5 U.S. cents. This would allow developers to also run local sales and promotions and support various micro-transactions, like in-app tipping.<\/p>\nWhile these changes will help to better target Android app users in emerging markets, Google made other improvements to app subscriptions, as well.<\/p>\nThe company said it’s making it easier to sell subscriptions on Google Play by allowing developers to configure multiple base plans and special offers, in order to reduce the overhead of having to manage an increasing number of SKUs as developers tweak how they want to sell subscriptions with offers.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter wp-image-2315603 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/google-play-subscriptions-base-plans.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1110\" height=\"706\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/google-play-subscriptions-base-plans.jpg 1110w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/google-play-subscriptions-base-plans.jpg?resize=150,95 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/google-play-subscriptions-base-plans.jpg?resize=300,191 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/google-play-subscriptions-base-plans.jpg?resize=768,488 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/google-play-subscriptions-base-plans.jpg?resize=680,433 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/google-play-subscriptions-base-plans.jpg?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1110px) 100vw, 1110px\" \/><\/p>\nIn this setup, a developer can establish multiple base plans each with its own billing period and renewal type — like monthly or annual auto-renewing plans or monthly prepaid plans. Then, for each base plan, they can create multiple special offers across the subscription lifecycle. For example, they could create an acquisition offer for a limited time free trial, an upgrade offer to move from a prepaid plan to an auto-renewing tier, or even a downgrade offer to help retain a subscriber who may be looking to cancel as they’re not using their full subscription benefits.<\/p>\nGoogle also offers an"https:\/\/developer.android.com\/google\/play\/billing\/subscriptions#in-app-messaging\">In-App Messaging API<\/a> that can be used to remind users to update their payment information when their payment method is declined, it noted.<\/p>\nThe company last year announced it would begin to support other payment methods, including both cash and prepaid plans. In the time since, it’s expanded its payment method library to include over 300 local payment methods in 70 countries, and added eWallet payment methods such as MerPay in Japan, KCP in Korea, and Mercado Pago in Mexico, Google said.<\/p>\n"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/google-io-2022\/\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/google-io-2022-banner.jpg\" alt=\""Read\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"At the Google I\/O developer conference today, the company introduced several changes designed to make it easier for Android app developers to generate revenue via subscriptions, particularly when trying to reach users in emerging markets. Most notably, the company said it will now allow developers to offer users the ability to subscribe via prepaid plans Play","slug":"google-play","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/32740565"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=32740565"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=32740565"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=32740565"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=32740565"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":18080603,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/in-app-purchases\/","name":"in app purchases","slug":"in-app-purchases","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/18080603"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=18080603"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=18080603"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=18080603"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=18080603"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2315386,"date":"2022-05-11T13:00:34","date_gmt":"2022-05-11T20:00:34","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2315386"},"modified":"2022-05-11T15:35:53","modified_gmt":"2022-05-11T22:35:53","slug":"google-play-adopts-app-store-like-features-including-in-app-events-and-custom-product-pages","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-play-adopts-app-store-like-features-including-in-app-events-and-custom-product-pages\/","title":{"rendered":"Google Play adopts App Store-like features including in-app events and custom product pages"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">At Google’s I\/O developer conference, the company rolled out a series of updates for Android app developers who publish to Google Play. Among these were two high-profile changes to its Google Play app marketplace, custom store listings and in-app events, which follow"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/07\/apple-to-introduce-a-b-testing-and-in-app-events-to-the-app-store\/\">updates Apple made to its own App Store<\/a> just last year.<\/p>\nGoogle had been offering A\/B testing for"https:\/\/android-developers.googleblog.com\/2015\/05\/empowering-successful-global-businesses.html\"> product page enhancements<\/a> since 2015 — a feature that allows developers to see which text and graphics would best convert users.<\/p>\nApple later adopted a similar feature when, at last year’s Worldwide Developer Conference,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/07\/apple-to-introduce-a-b-testing-and-in-app-events-to-the-app-store\/\">it introduced Product Page Optimization<\/a> designed to help developers to try out different app screenshots, videos and even app icons to try to appeal to different types of users. Developers could segment a certain percentage of App Store traffic to these cohorts to see which product pages performed better before deciding which page should be their default.<\/p>\nApple last year also announced a related feature called"https:\/\/developer.apple.com\/app-store\/custom-product-pages\/\">Custom Product Pages<\/a> that lets developers create different product pages to highlight different app features, each with its own unique URL to be used in external marketing channels.<\/p>\nToday, Google is following suit and essentially launching the same thing with Custom Store Listings.<\/p>\nInstead of simply testing different product pages, Android app developers will be able to make up to 50 custom store listings for their apps. Each page will have its own analytics and deep links available. Notably, this is more listings than Apple’s solution offers, which is currently"https:\/\/developer.apple.com\/app-store\/custom-product-pages\/\">set at 35 per app.<\/a> Google explains developers can use this feature to display different listings to users based on where they’re coming from. For example, a developer with a recipe-finding app could target ad campaigns to U.S. users based on U.S. holidays, by showcasing recipes for Thanksgiving or Fourth of July. But it could target users from other markets at different times with recipes related to their own cultural traditions.<\/p>\nApple last year also introduced an App Store feature,"https:\/\/developer.apple.com\/app-store\/in-app-events\/\">in-app events<\/a>, to allow developers to promote real-time happenings going on inside their apps — like special events or even just seasonal deals.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nGoogle Play is now rolling out its own take on this feature, as well.<\/p>\nWith the launch of what it’s calling “"http:\/\/android-developers.googleblog.com\/2022\/05\/play.google.com\/console\/about\/programs\/liveopsbeta\">LiveOps<\/a>,” developers will be able to submit content for featuring on the Play Store, including major updates for their app or game, in-app events and limited-time offers.<\/p>\nGoogle says LiveOps can drive 5% more 28-day active users to apps and deliver 4% higher revenue for those using the feature compared with those who don’t. The feature is in an invite-only beta testing phase for the time being.<\/p>\nWhile these changes were the highlights among those designed to help developers target, acquire and reengage their users, Google also"http:\/\/android-developers.googleblog.com\/2022\/05\/whats-new-in-google-play.html\">announced<\/a> a few other notable Google Play updates.<\/p>\nThe company said the Play Store would be updated to help people find the best tablet-optimized apps with new large-screen focused editorial content and a separate review and rating system for large-screen applications. Google Play will also later this year be updated to look better on tablets and foldable devices.<\/p>\n"attachment_2316998\" style=\"width: 1526px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2316998\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2316998 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-11-at-3.37.07-PM-1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1516\" height=\"988\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-11-at-3.37.07-PM-1.jpg 1516w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-11-at-3.37.07-PM-1.jpg?resize=150,98 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-11-at-3.37.07-PM-1.jpg?resize=300,196 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-11-at-3.37.07-PM-1.jpg?resize=768,501 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-11-at-3.37.07-PM-1.jpg?resize=680,443 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-11-at-3.37.07-PM-1.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1516px) 100vw, 1516px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2316998\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Google<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nFor developers, Google also"https:\/\/goo.gle\/play-sdk\">launched the Google Play SDK Index,<\/a> which lists over 100 popular SDKs and which app permissions they use, so developers can determine if they adhere to Google Play policies and help fill out"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/26\/google-play-launches-its-own-privacy-nutrition-labels-following-similar-effort-by-apple\/\">their app’s privacy labels<\/a>.<\/p>\nThe company said it will soon launch a new Play Console page dedicated to deep links to put all the information and tools for deep links in one place. It also improved its Store Listing Experiments feature (aka A\/B testing) to allow developers to see their results more quickly, with more transparency and control so they can better understand how long each experiment may need to run.<\/p>\nAnd beyond this, it rolled out features focus on improving app quality, including a new Developer Reporting API for accessing Android vitals metrics and issues data outside the Play Console; support for viewing vitals data at the country level; and Google said it’s making it possible to view vitals alongside Firebase Crashlytics. It\u00a0updated the Play Console by adding revenue and revenue growth metrics to"https:\/\/play.google.com\/console\/about\/reachanddevices\/\">Reach and devices<\/a> and overhauling its"https:\/\/play.google.com\/console\/about\/devicecatalog\/\">device catalog<\/a> to include install data and filters by new device attributes like shared libraries. It said it’s now easier to test apps on different form factors including Android Auto and soon, Wear OS.<\/p>\n"https:\/\/play.google.com\/console\/about\/keymanagement\/\">Play App Signing<\/a> was updated to use Google Cloud Key Management and the ability for any app to perform an app signing key rotation in the event of an incident or as a security best practice from the Play Console.<\/p>\nAnd finally, Google’s In-app Updates API will now let users know if there’s an update available within 15 minutes instead of up to 24 hours.<\/p>\n"embed-youtube embed breakout embed--video\" style=\"text-align:center; display: block;\">"youtube-player\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/embed\/d8mn0pmgvGw?version=3&rel=1&showsearch=0&showinfo=1&iv_load_policy=1&fs=1&hl=en-US&autohide=2&wmode=transparent\" allowfullscreen=\"true\" style=\"border:0;\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts allow-same-origin allow-popups allow-presentation\"><\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/google-io-2022\/\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/google-io-2022-banner.jpg\" alt=\""Read\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"At Google’s I\/O developer conference, the company rolled out a series of updates for Android app developers who publish to Google Play. Among these were two high-profile changes to its Google Play app marketplace, custom store listings and in-app events, which follow updates Apple made to its own App Store just last year.
